Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	This treatment often comes out; and if it does not come out, then it is extracted with forceps as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with forceps, it's good; if not, then extract it with a small incision and double needle; and if it does not jump out, then make a small incision in the ear and bite off the end of the candle or earhole, and fan out the part that is inside the ear wax so that it can enter with the ear; then the hole will be formed, as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, then take some lint and put it inside the ears, and do not use any instrument that can hurt it, and put a small piece of cotton outside; then press the wax with the wound or whatever it is, and make the hole.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. If it does not come out of all these things that we have said, if you continue to press on the ear even though it is swollen and spasms, and the manner of pressing if it is that you first sharpen the blade of the scalpel, and draw out the blood according to the strength of the blade, then hold the blade between your hands and turn the ear towards the opposite side, and make a small cut at the root of the ear where the fat is or the ear depends; and let the cut be as a moon, as you approach the point, then the bone according to your power, and the suction holds in your mouth; and the cure as it becomes healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is grain that is in and it swells, then administer the extraction; and if it cannot be emptied, then apply the suction gently according to this form.
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision on that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make the incision if you think the grain is swollen by moisture in the ear, until you have done it many times; then pull out the pieces with your fingers and with sugar, as we have said, if the extractions are allied.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the ear, therefore, that it is necessary to use the physician's hand in the ear, and open it wide with a piece of cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let's say on that same ear where the arrow is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps for that reason, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If it doesn't, then take several pricks according to the length of your arrow, and heat them; and put the salve on one side of the ear, and let it run down from there onto the other ear; and continue this pricking in the same spot until the arrow is completely out, and when it jumps, it will be completely out; and if you see, if you take one joint, and burn one of the bones in the ear, and the other bone hold in fire as long as the pain is the greatest; then make another part of other pricks as long as the arrow is completely out, until the pain is completely gone, as we have said in the prick.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the tooth, if it is small, like a pea and similar, it can be treated as we have said in the division; but if it is large, one can feel it, after adjusting the forceps; and this is the lighter thing to do in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of the ear rings from the ears, if you treat it as we have said in the division and use distillations, and the care is not effective if you look at the ear to the sun: if there are no holes, if you open them with subtle forceps, and if there are, if you take the noose of this form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be tight but wide and smooth.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And cut off the ear according to the amount of suffering of the patient, then form it into a cone; do this often as often as you can.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not yield to the pressure, then squeeze them into a cotton cone as we have said in the incision; and if they do not soak in as we have said, then apply distillations that the ancients have used in the decision of the verse, and you will find or mix your oils and medicines with them; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument, whatever form it takes, so be it:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	1. And let silver or gold be poured into the holes, and then strained through a proper instrument made of silver; and if you see take the receiver and wrap it around the pointed end of the cotton; then let your oil or juice flow out, and whatever you see of your medicines in the cauldron, and the cauldron should be in the ear; then blow gently through the receiver all over the cotton, and press your hand firmly until the oil is distilled or comes from the ear; and it will feel cold to the patient, and so is the distillation if it is not too hot; and keep it from being too cold, as the medicine will not be effective if it is.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the coldness of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some earache; and this same thing happens due to coldness of the ear, or a cut in the ear, and these colds never occur in the ear, if one cannot see; and no time has ever come when the pertussis was not seen, and it is well seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	1. That which comes in front of the ear, if it cannot be seen, is a sign of a serious illness in many cases; and when you see this, you must put the ear of the maiden in the sun; look closely: if you see the oedema apparent, then the swelling has completely covered this part of the face, and this is the form.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	2. And also and suddenly put your hand in front and behind everything, if it does not bleed the ear; if the oedema is of the cheek or neck of the ear, then take a gentle hold with your fingers, and lift lightly, as long as the pain is not too severe.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the tonsils are swollen in the ear, then take a soft, light rasping tool and gently scrape and burn a small part of it, then place it inside the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the inflammation that your ear feels is painful, carefully pierce it, and do not hurt the ear drum; then put a tent made of Egyptian ointment into the ear, and let it stay overnight.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not remove any wound as long as the pain is subsided, or if you put a tent and moisten it with pinkish ointment and powdered vitriol dust; and if you see that the ear is swelling, then take out the tent and move another soft tent made of rose oil and wax to cover it as much as it can swell; then cure it when it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	When the dislocation occurs, if a wet sponge is plunged and quickly cooled, and placed on the ear, and other treatments are used that are treated for the dislocation of the shoulder which are treated with distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the paper roll
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	That is the one that comes out of paper when the hairs are wet and dry, if you stretch them with needles and tweezers, and place on a piece of gypsum from its roots; then put the limb in a flask of vitrol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without cutting it, if the cautery is made with a subtle cautery lenticulaire, and the cauterizer after the incision is enough; and they are often repaired, none of their roots grow out; and when they are cauterized by fire, their roots are burned and do not grow back.
de la gresle	Of the greese
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times, things come in papers that seem gritty in form and hardness, and for this the disease is called "granule," and it is an assembly of large moisture in the paper of these and elsewhere; the treatment is as follows: first, if the granule is still on both sides, it is a light thing to know; then make it wide, then scrape each part lightly, then take tweezers, and close.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot feel the paper close with your fingers, if it does not hurt the patient; and if the assembly is large, if it is stitched, and the cure as long as it is healthy; and if it is small, if it does not make any force, because it restores the rest of the joint in order.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	When the snow descends towards the ear hole, if reversed, and the snow is grasped with tweezers, and the cloth is pressed from both sides; and if the paper is moved by incision, it causes no harm; when the snow is placed on the oil of bitter salt, and cures the limb that is misaligned as much as the malady allows.
de la graisse des eulz	of the grease of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that becomes entangled in the threads of papers, and this happens to more and more people, and causes pain to their hairs, and they come to the catharsis in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears are on their hairs; and for this they lie down with their faces turned away, and sleep, and their papers become wet with the exinach that the enflamement and appearance have caused.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	When you press on the joint with your hand and feel the exertion within it.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And how to open the joint if it is the patient's intention to cut through it; then take a cloth and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exertion contained in each part, then put it on; and press with both hands, so that the exertion is assembled within the circle; then make a circle of moisture at the wound, cutting a large notch, no larger than the wound you make at the point of entry; and make the cloth as wide as you can see the exertion; and in other ways, exertion comes from the notch, according to the shape of a greasy, pimpled piece.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	1. Pull the hair all around your body with a piece of cloth hanging between your two hands, and turn your left and right hands as much as possible; and make sure you do not pull too hard, so that you do not hurt yourself, and do not bleed.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	2. If the hair does not open at the beginning of the cut, lightly open it as much as possible when it appears; then pull it out as we have said, and then wet the cloth with water and apply it to the wound, and press gently.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	3. And if such men who bore their seal and put on to corrupt the moisture that is dried up.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the doctor when he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess comes to the eye, then the doctor uses soothing remedies as long as he is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of the paper's hairs
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers grow hairs other than their nature, and are wetted, if they harm the eyes, and bring about diseases such as common tears and softening of the paper and albumen, until it is caused by the destruction of the hairs; and the doctor treats according to four methods: either by burning together with fire, or according to medicine, depending on what is in front of or in the chapter of cauterization, and is made by cutting and stitching or by needles, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	1. It is necessary that you put the handle of the patient's arm in your mouth, then turn the paper of the oil to your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, then insert an awl into every hole of the file; and let the margin of the paper or the hair that comes from these hairs be on the left side of the paper, and turn the file to the right until all the hairs are aligned; then cut off the part of the paper that is opposite to the hair, adjusting the hair evenly, across the entire suture, from the largest to the smallest; then extract the file, and put a small piece of cotton and linen on the paper after the paper, then sew the figure according to the quantity that you see rising the paper that is marked with dots; and it should be like this.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If a part of the body has a wound that requires a large amount of paper according to its size, then cut out all the sheets according to the lines you have written, and start with a large sharp scissors at the beginning; and one of the holes near the natural hair growth in its enlargement by a root, then pull out the root at one of the two angles, then burn it completely; then assemble the two edges together with a stitch made with an awl to all the fine thread of the fabric, and take out the sand, and make air to the superfluity of threads on the two corners for anything gluing, if you see this done; and if not, then leave the stitch and the threads until three or four days; then cure the wound with the costure of things drying and constricting, because the paper relieves from the pain and assembly of the wound, but the costure is muedre (if it is said by the old one), and it is overrated with fear; and if in another way: and it is that you see the paper of a figure which is also like the felle of mirte, as we have counted, at three or four holes, according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then comes he who surpasses with equal force according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the nails, and the thing is not even, then take a needle or a thread of about the same size, and draw it through the hole; and take another thread of about the same length for the large arm, and a shorter one for the small, and assemble the threads evenly; then gently press with your hand evenly, and gently sew all the edges where you have made the cut, as we have experienced, then stitch the lips of the wound by sewing, and treat it as soon as possible; and if an abscess comes to your incision, so that it is relieved and calmed; and never has the hair of the paper been converted: if you use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching on both sides is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The patient's gums are cut in this way: and if you fold the paper according to what I have said, and then make the gums thus long and thin as the paper and the threads are; and hold the ends with the teeth; then assemble the two and the other subtly above the paper of the oil, and tighten the gums in the parts formed; and leave no corners, and the lip which is stretched will die and turn black and rot, as long as it hangs on it.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, if the force is great, then treat as soon as possible; and when the gum is healed, and if raised the paper, and no more hair will stick; and this is the form of the two gums you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and thin:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The first sentence to translate is: "The dislocation of the shoulder is such that you must use a fine needle, and a suture of silk fine and subtle; then assemble the heads and not knot them gently, and make the ends of the threads long; then order the other fine silk thread to be pulled through the chase, and not knot the heads; then place the malice's head in your mouth; and if the dislocation is to be seen, it is a subtle one and small, then pull the needle all through the chase at its root, and make it visible on paper as you trace over the natural hair; then pluck the hair until it reaches the chase, and pluck in the chase the hair, if there are I, II, III, or more; then withdraw your hand as the hair grows all over the chase with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	1. If the chase is treated and the hair does not come with it, then if you entrust the chase to the other end of the thread as you have ordered, as long as the chase comes out fuller and you see it through the sight of the oil; therefore, if you entrust the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two or three days, as long as the hair grows in its place and gives birth to the chastity; and if the hair is short, then accompany it with one long hair from the cheeks nature, and take it with the one you let go, as long as it is elongated and then tie it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the oil's fatness
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, known as "aleacrati" or oil coming, occurs in two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And comes from wounds, or cuts, or burns, and in similar ways.

And the way of the healing is to cut off the suture, and remove the lips of it, and put on bandages of linen, and leave it as long as it is sound; and nothing else should be used in the cure of it from things that dry and restrict.

de la char qui vient en l’oil	From the cheek that comes in the oil.

The accident comes from a wound and a burn and a cautery and things similar; and the sight of the eye when you prick it is that if you have a needle, if it has two threads, and the thread in the cheek, and it feels like a left lame, so that the threads come to the shoulder of the cheek; then the cheek is at the end of all the needle, and the cap at the large spatule.

dou soudement de la papiere	The paper should be soaked.

de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the bone of the elbow

des voines des eulz	of veins of hairs

de la fistule de l’oil	From the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	He examines the fistula of the oil: if it is cured by cauterization and by burning hot medicine according to what I have said, and it is not healed, then it must be opened at the site of the abscess, and all the moisture that is in it should be removed as long as the wound is visible.

puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide. dou derrompement de toile uvee	A sudden tearing of the eyelid

When a sudden tearing occurs in the eyelid, it opens wide and reveals paper like grains of resin; therefore, cover the eyes and the ovary is such that you can insert an awl at the root of the part that is swollen and painful, then insert another awl where there is a double thread in the part of the lame; and make sure, and leave the first awl according to its position; then cut the double thread and take a part of the eyelid, and twist it well, then remove the awl and put some ointment on a large amount of pus; and leave it until the threads are connected with the eyelid, then care for things that are comfortable for the wound as long as the wound is healed; and never leave the wound unprotected by the eyelid, as long as it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the hairs grow too long, if it is pricked at its base with a sharp instrument that comes from the oil, and the moisture is removed and the hair falls out, and it becomes healthy; then the hair is pulled out as soon as it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the oil's bowl
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not other than bowls assembled in the oil, resembling hot-flowing, and it is not hot; and the appearance of the dislocation if you make it seem that the patient lies on his side and straight, then take the head between your hands of II parts, and pull as much as you see the bowl coming to the desus at your hairs; then it is over, and it is clean and visible, and see the symptoms as they were; and if it does not descend, think that it is hot, and if the dislocation comes from the bowl is not assembled as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you place the patient's arm in your hands, then take a soft sponge and moisten it with the clear fluid on the corneal membrane; continue this until the bow is drawn out. When it is drawn out, if it drips into the cold, warm water or fenugreek syrup mixed with honey, or cold or fenugreek syrup alone, then treat it with other treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the appearances of water in the division, and when it is necessary to perceive; if according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	The translation of the first line is: "It is necessary that you place the patient's arm in your crooked hands, being towards the light of the sun, and the healthy and tight oil lies; then put the paper of the oil on your left hand so that the hairs are to the left, or on your right hand so that the hairs are to the right; then take in your right hand, if the hairs are to the left, the instrument called 'almagda', or in your left hand, if the hairs are to the right; then place the point of the instrument at the coronet through the opening of a ring in the oil at the smallest part of the arm, then push the instrument called 'almagda' gently, and twist your hand as it pierces the oil's ring, and feel that almagda enters the empty space; and the measure of the almagda's hole should be at the edge of the measure of the spice that is in the prunes near the end of the nose; and this is the coronet of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cornered skin, then put the instrument in the place where it is needed, and press the oil through a hole after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he becomes agitated now, if he sees the physician and the instrument before him.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After the patient has rested a little, and he becomes agitated again, open the second vessel, place the forceps with the instrument, and when it is firm and does not move, gently twist your hand around the handle several times; then take a piece of silk thread and lift the oil from the vessel.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then pour the oil into the wound, either rough or finely ground in oil of rose and a large amount of leeches, and anoint with the healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	1. Our, and those who are of our kind, place on with bread with much urine.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	2. And if it cannot enter the oil because of its hardness, since there are too many men with very hard hairs, then you must use the instrument called "alberit," which is shaped like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	3. And pierce only the conjunctive, and do not cut too much, but make a subtle incision, then extract the amagda as we have said; and at the completion of the operation, the patient should lie down on his back in the dark room; and let him have lighter foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and follow his disposition as much as possible; then leave him in this state for a while, and make him see some things, and then reinsert it as soon as possible on the ninth day; and it is only necessary that you do this in the eye of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you remove it because the inflammation increases rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When the patient feels pain, move the oil ahead of the seventh day, and address the one who calms the pain; and when they are calmed, remove the eye and put it in your face or on your forehead to cover any joint, and be careful in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then, go into the house quickly and convert yourself to your case; and advise that no disciples should intermingle in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And some came from the Yrach who told us that in some places it was made for the almagda perciet, but if one catches the fever, there is none in our land, nor do I know of any in the old books; and by chance, this is a new thing.
