Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And these are the heads of the several subtleties of this matter, and the tail is at third angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the char and the needle.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No chisels or needles are ever born or changed, and if they have any that seem like scorpions at the mouth of the pipe; and if they have a char enchanced with fuxe color, and if it is a char of bone color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these chisels which are not enchanced, and do not have fuxe color, it is necessary that you hold the patient between your hands before the sun; and work their noses, and grease the incisions on those chisels, and take them away; for if you do not hold them firmly in the subtle spatumile of one hand, until you see that the char is all out.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there is nothing else that can be done, and if you examine all the strumpets subtly and lightly, without causing any harm; and if you do not have any tools, or an axe, if you cut as it should be, and if the wounds are not infected, then cauterize as much as possible and let it dry out so that all the bones become hard and the wounds heal, then apply ointment or poultice.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If you can operate, and moisture comes to the palace, see that it is healthy; and if moisture does not pierce as it should, see that it has not caused any harm to the bone in the arm, or that the strumpets cannot be cut: therefore it is necessary to tie a thread around the tip of your finger, and it should be large enough for your hands, and there should be one between each nail; and put the malignant strumpet at the end of the thread in the mouth, and carry it around so that it does not stink; and often do this for the child as they go to school, and it is a light thing for him who sees it; then hold the chief that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other chief that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and let them pass one after the other without any pain.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	1. Do whatever you can to make the child believe that the dough has turned into a char, then take the boy's penis, cut the veins, and grease the penis with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in its place as before; do this 3-4 times or more until the ointment corrupts all that is left of the dough; then put a candlestick of plaster for some days as long as it is healthy, and if you have experience with drying herbs, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the child's head, or as we call it, distilling the oils and medicines or the candlestick.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or gold, resembling a hanging lamp, like a candelabrum, and guide it thus; and if you see, if it is a candle closed, and the wicks are flat to expel the wick; and it has a handle at the wick to hold it while heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the charcoal when it is cold
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times the head of the disease called "tetanus" is seen, which grows and becomes very large, until it is seen that something must be done at the beginning; then all the bones are cut off, and the hot cauterization or medicated ointment is applied; and if it is delayed as long as it is large, if it is hard, of a dark color, poor sense: if it does not touch metal at all, because it is enchanted, because when it is touched, no harm comes to the patient; and if the tetanus is of such a nature that it touches metal, not of iron, but of silver or gold, and you see that you can cover it, if you see that the patient's mouth is wide open and the hand is pale, and you can cure him of things dry and restricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the wound is cut and closed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	When a solution for continuation comes from one of these cartilages, it does not last long and is not found in any man.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to do this if there is no other remedy; look at whether the wound is fresh at its base; and then apply two legs of a garter, then treat it as much as it is healthy; and if the lips are already swollen on both sides, it is necessary that you scrape all parts of it as they become healthy, then assemble the two legs of a garter, extract it, and sprinkle some dragon's blood powder and incense on it; put some powder in a piece of soothing ointment container, and leave it until it dries, then treat the wound as much as it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing if you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the stomach sewing; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the lesions of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	The lips of the lesions have hard, grain-like areas that become more and more severe; therefore, it is necessary to treat the lips by turning them, each time cutting off a small piece, and taking them out with tweezers and closing each part; then use the leech after incising the veins, as long as they are not swollen; and then use the leech for drying things as soon as they are healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the chastity of the genitals
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	The chastity of the genitals has been pricked many times, which is what they call the "albulus"; if you can hold it with your fingers, and the root of the penis, and leave the wound or the vein; then put on the leather glove, or other restraining and desiccant powders; and if the chastity returns after the incision, and many times, if the root is second time, and cauterized: if it does not return soon after the cauterization; and these are the forms of the stums por coper.
des sordens	of the swords
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	1. No instances are gathered at the chief of the teeth, where the mouth is between the legs; gums that are swollen and harsh; and no instances are the black and citrus tooth and its root, as long as corruption comes to the gum, and it becomes the blackened tooth; if you intend to place the tooth between your hands, and its roots are in your holy hand, and open the teeth or the gums, as long as there is nothing more; and then make black and green, and yellow and other stains, as they are manufactured; and if this is in the first reason, it is good; but if not, continue to re-open the second day and the tooth, as long as you have everything back; and examine that the teeth have different forms of discoloration according to what the demonstration shows, because the rasor that whitens the teeth has other forms than those shown in the teeth; and these forms and others are with you apparent.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	1. It is necessary when you treat the patient's tooth pain that you delay your treatment as much as possible, because it should not be done; for it is a substance of high value, therefore there is no excuse for neglecting it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	2. When the patient is forced to undergo treatment, then you must be certain of the tooth's condition.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	3. Many times the patient's pain subsides, and ensure that the tooth is sound, and treat the tooth; and it will not leave the pain for long as long as the tooth is being treated, because we have already wanted to do this for these healthier ones; and when you are certain of the tooth's condition, if you must scrape off the tooth as much as possible, then use a piece of soft sponge to protect the gums of all parts; then the mouth should be your tool or have small hooks at the first post and post, as they are well inserted, then firmly fix the hooks; and the head of the patient's tooth should be well held in your healthy hand between your fingers, and it should be held so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the tooth firmly with the forceps, and if it does not break, then take none of these strings and pull out each piece lightly, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are seen and pulled out, then it is necessary to fill them with cloths, whether they are loose or tight; and if the extraction is done gently with needles, which does not break the tooth; and it is wise to cover the groin for cleaning the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be sure not to break it, and there will remain a part, and the patient suffers from the malice of the root, with greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	1. And you wear that you do not make it as they do who, by their haste and their hardiness, break the charm never, and they do not harm you anything that we have counted; but they bring it once by the aches of this great disease either by the roots that they desire, or by the broken bone, if often we want; and when it is raw, if you wash the leather with wine or vinegar and silk; and if they come out of the sang and water, which often comes, if you use the leather with vitriol ground; and if it is not, if you cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the wisdom teeth, or rather their points and roots, are long and wide, and do not double when you grind the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they are of large bones if they do not break when grinding, and are made of good iron, and are teeth that can be held tightly.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth.
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root of the tooth is broken, then you must put it in your mouth with wet cotton for one or two hours.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	as long as it is ground, then you will remove the tines that are called "alveoli," and they should look like a gum; and these are made in the same way as a tooth and are the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out of all these pricks, then it comes that you pull out the char entirely from the root, and put the instrument called "althali", which is a type of palinche, and its shape is as follows:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be large and thick if it does not break the skin, and if the root jumps by this, it is good; if not, then use all the instruments, and their shapes come after like this:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you need to use this instrument which has two rails, its shape is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front of the reason of the teeth, and this instrument which seems to be large thorns, its shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	1. And so it is that the force of the fracture may be broken, and the screws are made from the ends of the bones; and other screws, which are not quite as good, and the masters use their own instruments to make them, according to what their experience and the disease they demonstrate, because they have some diseases or the ancients did not teach any instrument for the diversity of the bones and their breaking point or other bones, or they perforate, if they seek screws that are necessary, which I have told you, and I will guide you with gestures, according to the form.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-holding so that they do not slip, but can hold and bear; then restore the part of medicines suitable for this, and if there is in the bone a fissure, and it is small, then use all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears to not fit with the natural body, and its form is misshapen, and even in women with many teeth, if you find that the teeth are not well after the tooth, and it is not right with the root, and it cannot be cut or carved: then remove it; and if it is attached to the tooth, if you use this instrument of which I have shown the form, and it resembles a small peg, and is of hard iron sawn into a point:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And how to handle a few teeth that are loose and wiggling, and because you don't move the others, and if it appears that one can be pulled out, then the tooth of a part of the tooth like this is formed:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is like the making of a pair of needle eyes; and in the tooth a few teeth are loose and wiggling slightly, if they do not move until they fall out; then the end is flat with no rasping, and the teeth are too sharp and they bend the tongue, if it is necessary to pull out the spicule as much as possible, if it does not bend the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth loosen by pressure or chewing, and the patient cannot press on them because of the pain they cause, and they should be treated with restraining medicines, and it does not help; if it is to be restrained with a golden thread, because the silver threads become green and rotten, but the gold does not move at all; and if the thread is too thick or too thin, according to the amount of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth, take the thread and the wire double between the two healthy teeth, then place the threads between the sick teeth, as long as you see improvement in the healthy tooth on the other side; then resume the covering where you started, and gently and wisely move your hand until it does not move at all; and if the patient's lip is at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then, the head of the child is held with nails, and they are assembled, and placed between the healthy teeth, and set in such a way that it does not cause the tongue to bleed; and then it is left there as tightly as possible, and if it loosens, or the string comes off, if it is tightened with another string; if it remains and serves for all its length, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the incisors of the healthy second teeth and the canines, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is removed, if it is reinserted into the gum, repeatedly, as we have said; and it does not become sore or inflamed, and never takes on the shape of a bone-like horse chestnut tooth, and it is placed in the gum where it is lacking, and if it fails, it is tightened as we have said, and remains for a long time:
de coper lou liien de la lengue	Of the copper wire of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No time is lost when the tongue is cut or cut off, which is necessary; or by accident from a wound; and the wires are such that they can open the mouth of the patient, and have their end in their mouth, and lift the tongue; then cope the nervous wire as wide as possible, until the tongue is loosened from its place, and if it bites or becomes crooked, and it is due to pain, if the tooth bites and cope widely the other side; and make sure that the wound does not become too large, for the artery is cut; and when you have done, if the gum is red and sore, or cold, then place the tongue on a linen tent; and the patient should be licked every night, so that the mouth does not become dry.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the dislocation occurs again, if the limb is quickly placed in the cold water; and if it does not heal, then the burn cauterization at the slow cautery, which is good for this, is made, and another treatment is done as soon as it is healthy.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the burn is not red or black and hard, if the patient does not feel it, if it is not touched, because it is a gangrene; and if it is declining into the bladder, and it has moisture, if it oozes pus, and the doctor makes a subtle spumous application, and delivers from one part and another; and if it does not heal in your care, then place the limb in cold water as much as possible, until all the swelling is gone. Then lift the limb from the castle and the other treatments as soon as it is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	gums of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Never comes the gums of the throat called "godath", and they are properly called "abscesses". When you treat them, as we have said in the division, if they are not healthy, keep them: if they are hard, of small size, and white color, if they are not touched by iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, if not touched by iron, then for the evacuation of blood; but let it be until it is dead, and then you will leave it, or it will break on its own; and if it is of blainche color and the root is subtle, if you have prepared the instrument with copper, but first look at whether the gums are chalz rested and calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	1. Therefore, place the patient in front of the sun, and make sure their head is in your hand, and they open their mouth and take the thread and pass it between their fingers, and press the tongue gently all over the instrument, as if it were silver or gold: and it can be made from fine silver or gold, like some threads.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	2. Can you press the tongue all over this instrument, and see the abscess, if you take the knife and the needle in the ginger, and draw it to the end where you please; and take no thing from the threads with, then close the instrument, as if it were made of silver or gold, that seems like strong forces; and all the limbs are twisted, and one place is another, and they are very tight, and is made of iron inde or of gall:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument present, if you have needles, then this is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	Then cut from one end and the other; and when you have cut one of the strings, cut the other in the same manner, and after making the incision, wet the blade with hot water, and make it sharp and smooth, and let the sutures come out if they are hot, or if scabs from pomegranate seeds are cooked, or if they are fueled with mirte, and such things; until the mouth is not swollen. Then cure it as it becomes healthy; and never have any other abscesses born in the mouth than the two strings, if they are cut off like the two strings.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with a small wound that affected her throat, it is to say an abscess; and she had almost completely closed all the gullet, so that the woman could not breathe through the clogged duct, and could not drink or eat, and died if she delayed for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had been drained twice through the two holes.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I removed it completely, and found in one hole a large piece of bone, and in the other hole a considerable portion of bowel; then I took another piece from the other abscess, and pushed the mouth and pressed the tongue; after removing the bone from this abscess and part of it, only a little blood came out; and then the woman was able to swallow water and wine, and continued to cut away the abscess as long as it did not close; and the abscess grew back, filling the wound I had made, so that it became very large; therefore I cauterized and burned the gullet: afterwards she recovered and I left these parts, and only God will do for me after this.
de l’uve	Of the uterus
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the uterus is drawn towards the vagina, and it is long and thin, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is very large and curved, it is called "uterus".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have described in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the abscess is quieted and subtle, and it is suitable to copulate; and the one that is curved is assembled and not long; and it is bloody or has a red or black color, and it is suitable to cut into the incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore, as you see, according to the method I have described, that you should cut the skin and flesh, that you place the patient before the sun, and press the lip on the instrument we made note of earlier; then remove the gallbladder through the urethra, and cut it into two segments, and sew them together with two stitches as I mentioned in the incision of the two eyes.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut too much, only the excess above the natural termination; for if you cut more, it will hurt your voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we said in the incision of the two eyes, and cure as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has pain in the other shoulder, then you must use an engine for the cauterization of the other shoulder.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cauterizing is to make it smoking hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the patient puts his head on your hand and then presses his tongue on the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter of cauterization, and confuses it with hot iron, if it is not too thick or too clear, and uses the edge of this instrument, then the form is:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has a hair on his head or puts medicine in his mouth, as if it were a pinch of salt, and places the instrument in all the medicine behind the eye; and the patient is giddy on his chest, if the saliva and mucous from his mouth come out of the medicine, if it does not reach the throat and neck, then hold your hand over all the medicine and press on the eye, as much as you can see and the medicine's sting is calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and pull the instrument out of the cotton through the loop of the cord, as much as the cotton dries on the eye; and do this often, as long as the cauterization is perfect, then leave it to dry, and after four or five hours or days, if you have the skill to re-cauterize the medicine, if it resumes, and after the cauterization of the discharge through the eye, wrap it in wool, and clean what is inside the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and cure gargles as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision alone. If it is treated with fumigation in this way, take calamus, ginger, origanum, rosemary, chamomile, and all sorts of herbs, and mix them together in one pot, and add water, and boil; and the mixture will be well glued to the earth, and the pot should have the instrument made this way:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or gold, and one of the heads should be inserted into the patient's mouth as long as the vapor rises up the urethra through the penis, until the urethra is blocked; after that, it often resumes, until the urethra dries, and make sure you do not do this at the beginning of the onset of priapism, as more things can happen; and do not do this unless it is during the decline of priapism.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a knife and cut the head of the catheter, if the mouth of the patient has not been too tight; for the catheter's head does not cause the vapor to scrape the mouth, and it is good for the patient's assembly salute.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened in the throat or spine of fish, or nothing at all; therefore, if you must see what is there, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing; and if you do not open it and it is stuck in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit otherwise than if the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if you manage to do this through vomiting; or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of gum, or a root of herbage, or a morsel of dry bread; and then wrap it around the sponge and then squeeze it; and when it comes to the mouth, if it sticks, and then pull it out; and if it does not come out of what we have said, then take the instrument of plucking according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	1. And let the sutures be placed at the head if it can more gently enter the mouth, and have the head raised; and guard that you do not touch the epigastrium, that all may live, and no bone be crushed; and it is best that the surgeon or assistant holds the instrument, because it is most likely to be held correctly; if it is let go, or it is drawn further along the instrument evenly, as far as it can be.
de la sansue de la gorge	2. of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	3. No time is needed for medicine, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when it does not benefit, look at the mouth of the patient to the sun, then press the tongue to the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	If you see the limb, if the bone is all fine and small, or if there are subtle needles that are worth this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this is not enough, then take a fine hair, and pull it out of the patient's throat, then pull or cut off the hair, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And make the patient drink this every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full mouthful of cold water, and open the mouth, and feel the saliva come out, and move it to your hand often; and if the limb feels cold immediately, then cool it.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if she does not understand as we have said, if the patient is smoking tobacco, with the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, as it feels good.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement. Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument used when treating wounds, if it is, when one can see, resembles needles with sharp points to enter the mouth; it resembles the beak of a surgeon, and has sharpness like lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot let go; and thus, the form is:
li chapistres des apostemes	The cautery of the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The appearances of the abscesses are, according to what is remembered in this book, and are diverse in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which one is in its own appearance, and that it is moist.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method if by the hands or if they are at the course.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the apostes of his head are different from those of his foundation, and the apostes of his limbs are different from those that come in jointures, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if an aposte is not perceived, as long as the bow is dead according to its completion; and if there are such cases where it is necessary to perceive when they are thought to be, and they do not die according to their completion, like those of jointures.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when apostes come from jointures, and they are left as long as they are porris entor, by chance if the ligament and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, because this is caused by contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	1. If the incision is deep into the limb, and you delay the perforation as long as possible, it will harm the principal limb; or if it is the foundation, if you do not stop it when it is almost dead, it will cause the foundation to collapse, and the fistula will be long and narrow, and it will not heal in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	2. And it is necessary that you clean the wound of the incision that is dead according to the completion, and when the pain is eased, when the fever subsides, when the pain and the bleeding are lessened, and when the debility and the fatigue are lessened, and other signs; and it is necessary that you close the wound or more dependent on the incision, and where it was opened; and it should be a long wound, and if the incision is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all of them equally or not.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those places where they prick, according to the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is present in the body, if it is necessary to leave the puncture as long as it is confirmed in digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you prick in this way before it, if the corse of the blood comes out from it, and it is painful to the mouth; and by chance they harden the lips and make them flat from it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is no abscess that is pricked according to the large vein, according to the member that it can endure.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	1. It is necessary that you carefully cut the small abscesses, small pustules; and in large abscesses, large pustules, and many flays according to the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses or they have to be cut away, and closed; when they become as hard as I am, and are dry, it is necessary to do so in the same way as one does with bubbles: and if there are such ones that are flayed at three angles, and if there are such ones that are flayed like the thorn of a rose, like abscesses of the gallbladder; and if there are such ones that are cut into a smaller size, and others in different sizes and appearances closed.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	1. If those who lack a caput, if it is only a superficial abscess, then you must open it gradually; and when the abscess is large, and the pus is thick, and it has entered the bone, then you must open it, unless you pour all the pus out in that hour, but pour a part; then the abscess stops, and the next day it opens again, and you do not pour anything else, as long as the bone is completely empty; at the same time, if the patient is weak in virtue, or if women carry, or if small children, or old men with decayed bones.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the expectors have never seen the end of the bowel, by chance died the patient, and you will not believe it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you feel the abscess, if the wound is small, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a small abscess, and it has many purulent secretions, then make tents of linen or cotton thread; and if it is large abscesses, and they have a lot of pus, then tie each one with a tent so that one against the other; and if you have found in the abscess a part of leather, and you have shaved it out, then fill it with fine cloth or rag of linen sense moisture, and the stitch, and the cure of ointment as soon as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the wound becomes infected in your shoulder, if you get sudden cold and wet, and many pain, and make the limb bend, and put it on the wound many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound persists, if it is not governed and cured, and the powders I mentioned in my hands in this book, and if you have fever, and the wound is nervous, then you should put on bandages and bend them with soft wine and ointment; and if it is like this, and the wound is hard, then you should put on bandages bent with cold and ointment, or with wine and oil hot, as we have said; and then take away the aposteme and the discharge and the cure, as it comes, until it is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it comes to pass that you understand completely in the treatment of abscesses: or you have said how one must go before the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of sore
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When severe abscesses come, and they are like us in their appearance, as the grape of a vine, and have similar appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	It has the appearance of being fat and large, or moist like a pig; and if it is of such a nature that it is hard and rough to the touch, and there is no doubt that the artery will not be harmed by it.

And the sections of size that you touch with all the instruments called "entromising," depending on the form that comes after, what it contains.

Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And it measures the incision scar and the wound, if it is smaller, because there are few sutures.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. In other incisions or wounds, the opening should be as large as possible at the most dependent part of the limb, to relieve the knee; and the cure should be done as needed.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times, the abscess comes to the neck, and loosen the girdles, and the wounds, and never have any other part or course, and they are mortified, and are intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly directed to its side, as if it were the abscess and the neck of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofula are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	It has several that contain moisture, and there are some that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that which you see of good disposition at the wound, and is similar to the color of the healthy flesh, and is not thin in any part, and is not rough as the neck of the head or the artery or the vein, and is not too deep; if it comes that you cut it with a knife, and burn it in some parts, and are the lips of the teeth as the gums, if you have mastery of it, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and the scar is small and few, and you are sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and are not too deep, that the hands do not slip, and do not see too far ahead, that you do not cut more than you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	1. If you prick the vein or artery, and it does not bleed, then put vitrol grits or any other powder that adheres to blood in the wound, and stretch the wound; and leave it until the inflammation is calmed and soothes the wound, and begins to ooze.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	1. If the wound is not cleansed, and it returns to its place, as soon as you complete it; then wait for your doctor's sign if it does not show any small pimples, such as scars and wrinkles.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	1. If the wound is a large pimple, then only clean it if you can reach the pimple at its root, but tie a strong double thread around it, and leave it alone without causing any harm; then apply an ointment of Egyptian linen to the wound, and cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you cover the entire wound, and manage to bring together the two lips of the cut, and hold them now, then there will be no excess due to the size of the wound.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you understand how to cover the root of it, and to treat it further, and hold it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez. de squinance	The first sentence to translate is "Ou caut
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The first sentence to translate is "Ou caut
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	The first sentence to translate is "Aces qui ont squinance, il covinet que li fendure de la gorge qui est appelee «epiglote» soit eschue; et c'on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the narrow passage, it is necessary to cover the epigastium to escape the destruction that comes from dislocation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epigastium, that we cut it at about three or four circles or one small cut through the cartilage; and then if it is possible to section the epigastium without damaging the liver, and the wounds are long enough, then.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the masters are not able, then it comes that the jawbone extends to the entire head, then cut the skin as far as the ear goes to the chin; and avoid the veins of the face, if you see nothing, and then cut the flesh, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the flesh that is broken off from the bone that is torn due to the fracture, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hour has passed since the injury, gather the two lips of the wound as much as possible, and touch all sides of the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote healing, as soon as it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim does not do this until the patient is completely unconscious, and the physician is judged dead, and the lack of hair.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, they cut the epigastrium because the physician cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and it is kept from death; and for this they commanded the physician to leave the wound open until the malady of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four. And therefore they commanded to sew the wound and cure it as soon as it was cured; and I will tell you what I see.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I see that a maiden is being cut, and she has a piece of cloth in her throat, and part of her clothing is torn; and I was called to cure her, and I found her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discover the wound, and find the blood that came from it, and though she did not have much strength or blood loss, the wound was in the throat, and it was through this wound that she died.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and treated the wound, and cured her as soon as she was healed; and she did not die until she was hoarse of voice, and returned after her disposition; therefore I say that in the tailoring of the epigastrium there is no great pain.
de la grosse gorge	Of the large jaw
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Hernia of the jaw is called an "epigastric hernia," and it consists of large hernias in a red color, and is often found in women; it occurs in two ways: natural and accidental; if natural, there is no engine.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident occurs in two ways: one is similar to fatty tissue, and the other is similar to hernias that come from the arteries; if there is pain, and it is not necessary to overdo it, it is better to use a small one, and prove and search for all the introitus: if you believe it is as fat as I am, and cannot be found in any way, if it is crooked, if it is like the ones we cut, and take all its contents, if there are none; and close it well, and cure it as much as possible.
des nous	1. "Of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	2. "There are many ways of us, all of which I will mention; and it is necessary to know the difference between a newborn and an outbirth.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	3. "I say that an outbirth is choler and fever, as long as the jaundice has passed and is completed with the digestion; therefore, the fever and choler rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	4. It is necessary, when you come to the cure of a newborn, that you first examine and search with all the instruments called "dislocater" according to what its form comes or chapter which is after.

The manner of examining the abscesses of the body is that you press or more moistly the part where the abscess is, and turn your two hands and hands as many times as you can until you feel that the stitch has caught the keur, then that is according to the size of the abscess; then take out the dislocater, and hold it in such a way that the thrust will be.

Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus. et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And he sets it on none of the bones that are strong against wounds and arteries, and never returns to this great form:

de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.
