dou chancre	The first sentence to translate is "dou
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division of the appearances of a chancre, and it is noted that one must overcome by medicines, and it is noted that iron must be used for the cure; and we say that the chancre enjoys in the marsals, and great caution in the cure, and they tell the ancient that when chancres are in the loins or can be treated if like the chancre which is in the mammary glands, and in the knees, and in the limbs, and it must be all done when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, if only you approach it, because I have never seen anyone cured; and no one has ever been cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. And the cutting, when it is in the flesh or can be opened, is that you never purge the cauterant with black lead; then make it healthier if there is manifest fullness, then open the vein with a knife to make the cut; then your bones will become soft or decayed, and all the hair will fall out, and all the nails will become loose; and leave the wound as it is, and press well on the place with your hand or with nothing, and if they dislocate from the wound, it is because the cauterant has been applied too much to the artery or vein, so that the flesh is not anesthetized; then another treatment is needed as soon as it is healthy.
de ydropisie	The first sentence to translate is "Ou cautere de
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	The first sentence to translate is "Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’ils soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And so proceed with the second part.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And so proceed with the second part. At the point, and if you do not see it enter only as far as the intestine when you touch it, and it cannot be cut; then look if the hydrometer is in contact with the intestines: if it comes that you cut from the abdomen, the third must be done straight above the point of puncture; and if it is due to liver disease, then the cut must be made at the third from the right; and if it is due to mucus, then it must be made at the left, and not more than the bile ducts do not flow to the weakest part of the liver; then perforate all the skin with the instrument, and the bougie, and ease your hand over all the squamous tissue between the skin and the fistula as you would when scraping a piece of wax or as much as it comes out to the left four, and that is the end of the abscess, then pull out the instrument, and if the bougie is of the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a silver needle, and is of iron or light wood, and in its part nearest to the little puncture; and on one side, three punctures; and on another side, two, and one; and it is the head cut so as to be like a quill, and is the shape of the incision that the scribes make with the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the head of it is the axe, so that when it is struck by the edge, if it bends now under the instrument; empty the part which is the first or third, for if you see more than it should be in that hour, by chance it may die from the resolution of its spirit of the arm, or it may have cold hands, or it may be near death; but according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of his virtue signify, and his courage; then take away the instrument and hold the edge, and it is held now by the heat which dries the puncture which was sawn by the sycamore, according to what I have spoken, that you perceive this way; then resume the instrument another day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and take a small quantity of astringent; do this every day, and keep it from being too long, until it does not more but has a little astringent.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	If you doubt the patient's condition and do not provide relief, then the cure for the grave or sandwound is to let the patient drink water or bath and in the sun, and the sign of thirst; and the cure of drying medicines as soon as it is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and liver and spleen after the extraction of the wound, just as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the tooth
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Never have children been born who did not have a toothache in the gum, or if it is small, or it is not present in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If the patient is not able to perceive anything at all, even the slightest subtle thing according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place the catheter subtlely and tie it with the thread, and leave it for 3 or 4 hours, and when you see that urine is coming out, if it does not close, then remove the catheter; and by chance, no one will be closed, because the urine that comes out will not close.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the catheter is small, and it is treated with a tight clot of thread as we have said, then if it enlarges.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the catheter in their groin are bleak, because no one has the catheter at the tip of the penis, since they cannot urinate before they lift their penis up; and they cannot ejaculate because of this, because the matter does not come out quickly enough, and it is a very serious disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. And the manner of the cauterization is that when the patient suffers from soreness on his back, it is the head of the thorn and the point is like the size of a pen's tip, if it pierces through the skin, if possible; and keep away from the loss of blood that comes often, and if it happens, if the wound is cleaned and cured as soon as it is healthy.
des pustules de la verge	1. of thorn's pustules
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. Many times they come out in the thorn, and it has a disgusting appearance; and among them are malignant and non-malignant ones; if you burn them at the subcutaneous fat, and cut and clean them all, then put on cotton wool soaked in Egyptian ointment; then the treatment of ointment diaconicon as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	If the tumor is malignant, of a putrid smell and size, then it comes that you must use cauterization.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	After you have cauterized it, and if the tumor is still in its early stage, and has part of its skin and hair, then it comes that you must cut off the part that was skin; and when it has healed, if the hair grows back.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you cut it off in one piece, if you do not secure the head of the tumor, and it is not perceived, then blackness and corruption come to the part that was cut off; then everything that is black and corrupt comes out, then apply the plaster of honey and flour made from the scraps of roasted peaches and vinegar, then other treatments as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if the evacuation of blood comes, then follow this form of the lunar cauterization:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if the evacuation of blood comes, then follow this form of the lunar cauterization: It is knowledge, at the discharge of blood, and at corruption; and if the head of the thorn is corrupted and retracts, if it happens that you bind or lead the thorn with a cord, and pierce the malaide through; and when the pelts are drawn to the root of the thorn which has come to these who have not been circumcised, or have been injured or infected, then it comes to pass that you scrape it with the instrument's blade, as long as the lips are slipped, and are released from the thorn's root through all parts; and if this is a difficult matter to do, then you scrape it in the spittle of any part of the thorn and the hair; then apply some element between them, and put a subtle drapery of wet lin on the cold needle, so that it does not pierce again.
de la circoncision	Of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the least of wounds if it follows others; however, when we perform this work out of our own will and for the benefit of our children, and properly as it should be for them, and the most gentle for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not call circumcision of their children because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have the greatest part of masters and physicians who performed circumcisions outside the del, with force, and on all occasions; if it were not for the knife, which has many edges, and by chance if one cuts more than he intended, and moreover if one cuts too much.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	When the wound is cleaned, and there is double pain, and the circumcision that is not properly secured is not sure of the point of the member; and the circumcision of the finger by chance escapes the iron, and cuts the skin, and often does not grow out, and many times are born without any need of circumcision, and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the circumcision that is made with force, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut both ways, as well as above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, if it fits well in I, but that the thread is not too thin; and that the manner of the first cut is such that it seems to you that the child understands, that you do not pull the thread too much, only when the verge, and then pull it straight between your hands or your fingers that the children do not see, nor any of the strings; then put your hand on the verge and blow or keep it, and lift it as high as the head of the verge is assembled, then make a good mundification of the waste that is assembled, then tie the leu signiet of a double thread, then tie the other lien to the other lien; and tie the knot between the two pouches and the dot, then loosen the grip very quickly and lift the head of the verge; then leave the sanc poc and poc, for it is the most evil; and put some powder on and powder the powder with a piece of cooked beef cut in small pieces, confited with olive oil and fresh, and leave it suspended over the other jar, and the cure is done as long as it is healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces at the body's end is this: the two heads are thin and long, and are as strong as the fingers equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of mummification is when the hair escapes at the incision; therefore, it is necessary to extend it to your nail, and if it does not cause an abscess, then the covering is well done, and if you do not hold it with your nail, then the covering will come off.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it passes three years, and the fringe is shrunk, if you allow it to be as the abscess is calmed, and gently burned, and if the covering is as you hold it from the part of the fringe, it will not harm you.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	The first line of the translation is: "Cure the joint with something that has been treated with powder, as we have said or mentioned about powders, and if it is not too much measure, it will go away, if it does not hurt; cure the joint, as we have said, as soon as it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	The second line of the translation is: "Hold back the urine.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The third line of the translation is: "If the urine is bloody, or frozen, or bowel, or gallstone, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is discharged, and you see that it is retained by the urethra, which is at the anus or collar of the bladder, then it should be held with the urethra against the back, and the belly is extended from the part below the back, and restrains the urethra as much as possible; and then the urethra of the bladder is constrained to the expression of the urethra at the desire of the urine, if it is discharged, and if it does not come, if we have said, and the urethra feels great pain, then it should be administered an extraction with all the instrument called 'siringue', of which the form is: and it should be fine silver hair, as thin as the tail of a squirrel; and it should be the tail of a palm tree about half a foot long, and it should be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Here comes the translation:
des maladies de la vessie	Of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are scorchings or abscesses in the bladder, or when purulent matter is assembled, and you see water and medicines being distilled, then do this to all the instrument called "clepsidra", and it is shaped like:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it is third degree: two parts of one, and one part of the other, as you see; and it is read by the medicine that is such that it burns well the verge without addition, if you can draw the moisture, and bind when the job is done; and when you see your medicines gushing in the bladder, put the end of the cord in the moisture, and draw it to the drawing which is therein; if you draw the moisture from the stringer, and then hardly pull the drawing therein; if the moisture enters, and comes to the bladder now, if that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle clyster in which the bladder is clisterized: if that is so:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	1. It is made of silver or archaeal, and the head is higher; 2. Take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture that you see clysterizing it, then place it between the two sides to form a double-layered pouch, and heat the moisture on the fire; 3. Then cut off the clister at the end, and hold your hand steady on the bladder until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; 4. If you don't have the bladder, take a piece of linen, make a circle, and pierce it roundly through the holes; 5. Then pull out the strong wire tightly in these holes, and assemble the circle as you would an anvil, and put what you see oil and moisture and sage in it, and tie it with the instrument; 6. And do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	Of the incision

de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the hairs

Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that all abscesses come out by cutting or by arrows; and this is by case.

Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	For this reason, do not hasten to perjure yourself, but make sure the pain is soothed; then place the patient on the table, and have two assistants hold him down while you support his back and assemble his limbs as they fit the leg; let his fingers be expanded, and put his knees at the groin, and tie them well with a gut string; then move the instrument towards the left side, and after that comes the form of the mouth, and it is necessary that when you see the instrument being placed, you fix the first part to know the fitting of the mouth, so that whatever enters through the instrument does not fit more than it should, and does not harm the patient; and if it is larger, then it is necessary to cover the fitting of the mouth with cloths, so that the patient is not grieved; and it is necessary that the instrument's horn be placed at the end, and that it be drawn out.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	When the abscess opens and it is cut with a clean hand, if it covers the head, apply rose oil or olive oil to the wound; when the boil is visible, place soft tentacles in the wound with oil, and put the tent on the mast and the point of the nail clean and rough with vinegar or bitter herbs that are cooked; then the cure after two days of dressing as it becomes healthy; and never lift the head and the wound with a cloth of vinegar and honey, and then with vinegar or the roots of lis and aristolochum that are cooked; then continue the treatment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is dressed in the marsh, then it comes that you must not cook with iron, but cure as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Mastery is first in the dance, to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs if you see the woman press upon her abdomen, and desire to smell the aroma: therefore, help the children to come forth; and then assure yourself that these children are according to the natural figure, and are from your loins, and the second one with him; and when you see these signs, it comes to gently press upon his belly, if he will soon be born; for when he descends from his head, if he is with his second one, and is monied by good cleanliness, and that which comes otherwise is not natural.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For there is no time that it comes to his bones, and it comes to the heart or the head, and the hands, or it comes to his belly or stomach, and it is converted by chance or his collarbone, and by other malicious figures; if it is skilled in the dance and wise and subtle in these things, and warns against error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures of what one must help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out of its natural place, and the woman gives birth painfully, and the virtues of the child are weak, if it is placed on a pillow or the women hold it; and let its nature be like olive oil or fenugreek, and then dance between its two little spatulums, which is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	1. "And open the second, and push it against his nail as much as the moisture that is in it will allow; and then press the belly of the woman as much as the children descend, and if they do not descend, then it comes to clamping the woman's thigh with flaxseed oil; then place it and secure it with thread, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: if it is now time for the children.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	1. "And if the hands come out further, then it comes to lightly reset them a little at a time; and if they do not go in, then place the woman on her side, and lift her feet up; then lower the side on the ground, and mark on the woman that she does not have any pain standing; and if the hands cannot be set further, and the children are dead, then press the hands against the angle that is here before you, extract the child, and reset it as equally as possible.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	Of the child's foot that has its toes
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes to its feet, if it is possible to wear them high; and then the shoe is gradually tightened as much as possible; then he puts on the shoes and extends them slightly.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Can it leap high jumps, if commanded to wear them, and the other is fastened with conduis; if it leaps, may God help it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not leap if we have said that it should be tightened a little, as much as possible; then it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For it is light.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	If it does not come out as we have described, say if you need to use muscular force of the arm, oil of sutures, and melted gum, and put on this remedy according to the nature of the woman's labor and firmen this application, then fasten it tightly in a cold cloth until it reaches the ribs; when it is moistened at the ribs, make a bandage of iron wire, and insert it, and leave it for an hour; then fasten it on the seat, then draw it out and press the mouth and nose, and press lightly on the stomach because the child is now jumping.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	The issue of the child from its loins
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if the mother holds her hands close to her neck; then she should tie a string around her neck and hang the baby's feet down, and hold it tightly; and she should fold her hands close to her belly, and press her elbows against her belly, as far as the knees are apart; and if the child does not jump, she should take her elbows and make them form a V, then she should make her belly move forward, and then hold the baby's feet; and she should hold the baby close; and command the woman to pray as long as the child is like this.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the child's birth that comes out of a hand wide
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I must have an engineer to bring the hand: if I cannot bring it, then lift the woman, and go; if she cannot go, then make her sit on the bed, and straighten the legs; then relax the muscles that I have told you about; and if it does not give birth, then make her sit on the seat, and study to bring the hand back; and when the child is born, make it natural, and make it smaller, and command that it presses as much as the child can.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the child's birth at its neck, and has expanded its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	1. It is necessary that the wound stains the hand, then it should be turned a little and a little, and lightly; when it is even, if it is applied with the nature of mustard and oil, as we have said, then it is commanded to move a little and a little; when this is done, if it is held in place at the seam, and it is commanded to press; and the seam is tightened.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	2. In the same manner for all the rest.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	3. When it comes to using this method for all the rest, if the second time is applied to your nail, as long as the moisture is dry; and if the children can reach their face and neck, and the blister bursts, it should not be held, and it will hurt the child; then cut off the blister as soon as you have done it, according to how it should be done, and command the woman to press no time: therefore, if it is done lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	The issue of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is rare for twins to be born multiple times, and never without one being born alive; and this is a strange thing that has not been seen before.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	It is rare for twins to be born multiple times, and they do not survive; I know that they are multiplied, and are shaped by the fate that decides them, which is linked to the bow; and they never issue naturally like all at once, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born gently, if the cure is as we have said, and it is the delicate dance, and done quickly and lightly what it does; and done as it should be for salutation.
de plusors enfans	Of more children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	No times are formed in the marriage I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more than XV, and they are all formed as a child by the measurement of the girl's growth, and cover that the dance is all that comes, because by chance it seems to be something like that; if you do according to what is said.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	If you treat the woman of the dead child as I have said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are forced to cut with hands; if it comes to pass that the woman is of sound health and has no accident or death; if it comes to pass that the woman is lying on her back and her shoulders are curved downward, and her knees uplifted; and the midwife applies the teigne of II parts, or she lies in bed if she is not treated for the descent of the child; then anoint the mouth of the mother with oily oils with musk and camphor and linseed meal, and anoint her hands with these oils and oils; then blow lightly on the mother's hands with these oils and oils; then take the leu or the bones that are loose and put them in the mouth of the mother, and watch if the child is descending from its head; if you see the bones in her fingers or in her throat or in her mouth or in her hair or on her chin or in her beard or in her cheek or near her eyes, and the bone is seen in her left hand, and puts the crown between her two fingers of the right hand, and blows it lightly to all hands, and does not touch the bone in any of these ways that we have mentioned, until it comes to pass that it returns to the empty thing; and this is the form of the bone:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then find the other bone, or if you have skill in it, if the extraction is equal; and then the joint moves equally when moved from both sides, by using your teeth to hold it, as shown in the figure.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	If a part breaks off, if there are any of its two bones missing, and the other part is pulled out, and the remaining part is treated; and if it does not break off, then put this bone or higher on the leg, and do this until all of it has been removed.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by stretching, then it is necessary to wrap it around as shown in the figure, until it is completely stretched; then the cloth is placed at the joint of the plantar or the toe, and then you do the same with the other hand, and take off the foot.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	1. If the child's head is large and it is misshapen at the end, or if there is a sudden assembly of the fontanelle, then you should insert the spatula with pricks between your two fingers and cut the fontanelle and extract the moisture; or you will do it with the instrument called "almidach", which comes with the forceps or chapiter that follows after it; and then naturally make the child's head large; and then pull out the bones with tines, and if the child's head is forced and held in place by the force, as long as the moisture that comes out is not too much, then it will be held in place; and if it cannot be released, if the piece is made from the pieces you have, and if it is enlarged in the belly or deformed at the costal cartilages, then you should percute as much as the moisture comes out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	If the child is on its mother's breast, if it has a light attraction, and the suckling goes to the mother's mouth, it is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If the child is in the belly or the pudenda, if it covers that you draw it out at the side with your hand; and then the belly or the pudenda, as much as the moisture which it has received; and if the other limb is osteit, and the shoulder is demoure, then bite your hand with the mouth of the mother, and draw it out; then the oncine or the two, and draw it out; and if the mouth of the mother is retreated because of the aposteme chaut which it has come, then do not make any trouble, only manage things that are moist and heavy; and the management emplaustres, and sie in aigue mollifians et amoistans.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its chest, and you place it evenly, then follow what we have said in the living child; and if there is no problem, then the part that is broken will be replaced by pieces, and nothing of the second part will remain.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if the child is broken as we have said in the appendices that come with the marriage; and if the wounds come, then if it is made acute by restricting the poultice, and the child is further injured.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly some children had died, then consulted another of this, and it turned out that she would die as well.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, some apoplexies came to the head, and they inflamed as soon as they were seen, and began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for the cure, and I thought it would be long, and I could not relieve the pain.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I used strong means of firm attraction, and after a while, some bones were broken, and then more and more.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was surprised, because the stomach has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If you thought that it was bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I wished for the pain, and I cut the bones as long as the woman was in better condition; and I saw the woman in long pain for a little while, and it was because of this chapter that, when the master did something strange, I thought I could help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To bring the shoulder back to its place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Then comes the form of pressure, with which we press the books; and when it turns, it turns the shoulders.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Whole, the corners must be more subtle and restrictive, and should be made of flat or square wood; and the mouth must be about one-third the size of the eye, and the margins of the branches one-half a palm and a half; and the two joints should be two hinges of this same kind, which are closed on one side and open on the other, half a palm or more; and these two hinges are fitted in the mouth of the shoulder to open when we turn the corners.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter, can be made of flat ebony or boxwood, according to the appearance of the nails; and it has two arms, as you see, like a palm of the hand, and they are wide; and when you open the marriage bed with all the instruments, if you place the woman on her side and the legs overturned, then adjust the arms together in the marriage bed, and hold the head of the instrument between its handles; then operate your hand on all the instruments, as you have done with the nails evenly, according to the quantity you see open the mouth of the marriage bed, until it fits as it was.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	1. This instrument is of various shapes and sizes, and they resemble each other in appearance; when you have seen them, the more you use them, the more you will understand their value for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	2. If you do not know the instrument that you have not seen, because its needs are not easy to understand.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	3. dou fremit	4. "If the wound moves
