de la voinne civile	of the vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in the ground where there is no moisture; and by chance it may be found in other places than in the legs, and this comes from the fat that comes from the skin, as it does from the serpent's belly and turns, it is found between the skin and the char.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if signs of the beginning of this wound appear, it is that there will be a very large inflammation in the leg, then it changes color, and the wound begins to ooze, as if it were a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	If the wound is opened, it comes to pass that you wrap it around with a piece of cloth from one and a half inches to two and a half inches wide, and around the leg, and leave the cloth there until the wound is no longer red, if the cloth covers the wound and the now, and if it is too long, if you cut off a part and wrap the remaining part around the wound, and do not cover it with another piece of cloth until it is all used up; for if you do, it may cause infection and gangrene or putrefaction of the flesh, and for this reason it is necessary that it be treated as little as possible and quickly, and there should be no remaining part of the wound after it has been treated with V paumes of long, or X, and I had one such case where it was X paumes long, and if you wrap it, if you see any holes or perforations, and the cloth presses against the flesh, then all should be cut off; and whatever matter is decomposed, and all medicines are avoided for food, then the cure is performed like the apostemes.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And no time the hands are wet, and at the same time when it opens in the joint of the shoulder or the other, and a drop of blood comes out, and it falls; cure the patient as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of those that are born between leather and hide.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our country "beef disease," because it often occurs on the shoulder and is a small worm that runs between leather and hide, going up and down the body, and causes pain in all parts of the limb, as it goes through the skin or not, and jumps; and it is caused by some humors, such as snakes, worms, and ascarides or intestines; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the body, it goes to the head, and enters the oil, by chance, and destroys the oil; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see the wound healing and drying, if it cannot be otherwise than when it will: if it comes to pass that you read the leg and bone, and cut them as closely as possible, then sew it up and leave it, and it will heal, if the cauterization by fire is done as we have said, until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does, if it comes to pass that it reaches the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming towards the oil, if the hair is drawn back from it, then sew it up, and leave it; and it will heal. And it is necessary to use the caustic with the mouth of medicines soluble for the humors of the body, and avoid foods that are injurious to the stomach as nourishment.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes from ventosity
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakitir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to certain members, and spreads from member to member; and I see what I have told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called a woman patient, and I saw my arm, and I saw a small flesh in the vein of the other arm; and then afterwards, I saw it rise as if it were a snake to the shoulder, faster than anything, as if living silver when it cut from there to another; the pain left that arm and moved to the shoulder, and then a little later, it spread throughout the body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that she dislocated it further inside the chest, just as I see.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I am surprised to see it move from joint to joint, as I have never wanted this disease to occur in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Indeed, I wanted to prevent any discomfort in the joints, but I did not want this. In fact, it is because I see it in women; I thought it was because the woman had dry skin, and the veins were exposed, and because of this appearance of constraint; but I did not know that this is true for those who are delicate and have moist skin and veins replanted.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see the cure for this disease, and the patient feels pain, if it opens as we have said, if the ligaments and bones are well-matched, and then continue until the constraint in the joint is reduced; and cauterize the joint; and if you do not see it with your eyes, if the cure of those who cause the constraint is like the fetid pills and serapeum pills, and similar ones.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their appearances and according to the muscles of the body where they are located or they cause pain.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of arrows includes those with large points, and small ones, and sharp ones, and blunt ones; those with angled edges, and those with curved shapes, and those with pieces; and those that pierce any member in different ways: either through the principle member, such as the head, chest, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, uterus, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	If the arrow pierces any of these members, and you notice the signs of death that I will tell you later, it means that you should not remove the arrow immediately, as death comes later in other ways; and if the sign does not seem to you, and the arrow is not far from the wound, then the hole should be cleaned and the wound treated.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	The patient experiences severe headache when the arrow pierces the bone, and the sudden shock that is felt in the eye is when there is scotomia and dizziness, and vertigo and pain in the limbs, inflammation and soreness of the tongue, spasms and mixture of understanding, and vomiting of cold; and by chance it does not affect the nose or ears; and by chance it affects the speech and voice; and a sudden shock of the white wound-like scar resembles pustules, and like the bite of a horse; and this sign appears if you seek treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is still inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the shoulder when it pains or aches is that it is near the left breast, and it feels as if it is twisted in something hard, without being empty; and by chance the shoulder becomes as stiff as the leg, and in a short time dark blood comes, and there is cold sweat and cold blood, and convulsions: then one feels doubt that the death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arm that is swollen is that there are no plains of ecchymosis from the wound, and the throat is swollen, and the face turns pale, and he spits up blood high and cries out with pain.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the shoulder is dislocated in the covering of the chest, it can cause the small ribs; and it causes great pain and suffocation; and all the members of the shoulder move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the shoulder is dislocated in the stomach, by chance, jumping from the wound nothing of the meat undigested.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the shoulder is dislocated in the stomach, and by jumping point of the intestine out, if there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the shoulder is dislocated in the bladder, and the urine jumps and comes out, and the patient feels great pain: dying wounds.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if the face and neck and shoulder and arm and spine and back and ribs and chest and thighs, and the seeming member, are safe according to other dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the artery is in the wound or not visible, and it is not bleeding, as I will tell you if I know, because you are doing this.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I have seen one man's arm cut off at the elbow by a knife or an axe: I tried to save it, and the graisse of the ear was removed successfully.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And there came to him a sudden pain in his arm that he fell into the grease of the oil, and the arm was set, and it could not be reached beyond the shoulder, and it was as large as a Turkish bow, at all times making him feel light-headed with his ears; the shoulder was healthy, and he did not have any accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And there came to him a sudden pain in his neck from a collar, and it was the Arabian collar at the ears: I was the beard, and subtle as much as I could see it, and it was healthy for the crestians.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And there was a wound on his body, which he thought would kill him; and then after 30 days, if it had not changed its position, I opened the wound, sewn it up, and dressed it, and there was no sign of an infection.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	If a wound is on the thigh or back of a man, and it becomes infected, and the wound does not heal, and does not follow its natural dispositions, and does not find any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if another man has a wound in his face, and it becomes infected, and he suffers great pain; and then after a while, other similar things happen.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I found a splinter in the side of the king's man, who had it stuck in his hand; it was a small one, located on the left side. It remained there for three days before I was called to treat it.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound that was tightly closed.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I tried to open it very gently, and I did not feel anything; but I felt a sharp and painful sensation in my left ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the splinter I had placed in my hand, because it did not burn; and I seemed to feel that it was the splinter.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I place the splint on the hand, and relieve the right-side wound, and wait for the surgeon to extend his hand long enough so that he can touch the elbow of his arm; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied the medicine to the corrosive wound on the hand, as it was overgrown, and touched it, and felt the elbow of the thumb that was bent towards the fingertip; then I closed the opening of the wound with this medicine, as the head of the thumb appeared visible to me; and it healed well in four months, and then I removed the stitches, and the sutures from both sides, and could not; therefore, I continued to refine and invent ways to strum the strings, as soon as I had well-made stitches, according to the form that will come at the end of this chapter, as I stretch it, and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physician judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it accordingly, and the wound was sore, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I said the quality of extracting some arrows, if you apply your cure to what I do not say, because the books cannot make everything appear perfectly; but the masters of the art make great things with few tools and the things that are present and lacking, they achieve nine works and nine instruments in the descent of the things drawn down this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not issue from the limbs or they are bitten for the following reasons: either by the leg or they enter, or in another way; and the one that is thrown from the arm or it enters, it is an arrow that has entered into the flesh, and it will never be thrown again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	If she does not jump now, if she lets it be entirely exposed and the wound is open, and she becomes fixed in the bone, and she cannot move if there are no other joints, and each joint is closed; then she jumps, and if she jumps, if she perceives through the wound at all points, as long as the wound is eslargied, and then the trai.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is fixed in the bone and waits until one of the stomachs of the eye, and some of the accidents I have mentioned open for the patient: if not treat it, but leave it as long as it remains even after some joints, because if the arrow comes to syfac, it is the death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	When the bone is not broken only in the bone itself, and does not come out of its place, and no other accidents have happened to the patient, then the surgeon should intervene.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bone is already broken and cannot be set, then the surgeon should immediately provide first aid, as I have told you; then treat the patient until they are healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	If the bone is not visible in the limb, and the patient insists, then use any instrument you have; if you feel it, if there is no wound or injury, then treat the wound as much as possible; if the ear is large, and the ear is held by the bone, then cut or crush the ear of the limb as much as you can; but be careful not to cut the ear too much.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not once, if the child until it is read has been harmed, then tear it, for the extraction causes pain.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the dislocation of the shoulder is against what we have said in this chapter, then you misunderstand what we have said in this chapter; and you will be cut on the nerve and vein, and it will be sewn according to how you think you can remove the arrow without causing further harm, either quickly or slowly, or firmly or gently; and you will sew the skin according to how it was when the arrow was removed, because this is the largest help that can be given, and if you do not, if you do not, then follow what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The first line of the translation is: "The arrowhead that comes from another part, or it does not open anything of it, or the leather is bent in some place so that one can see or feel it differently: then pull it out, as much as the points can hold, and then extract it: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, if you turn your round hand around as much as possible when it enters the bone, and widens the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be drawn out, if you leave it alone, and then continue the extraction as much as possible when it is drawn out; and if it is the arrowhead and it is in the shaft, it is cut off at all ends; and if it is the tip of the arrowhead and it enters the hair of the instrument, and then it is cut off, and if the arrowhead is hair, it is cut off at the point entering the instrument for lighter extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrowhead is stuck, then it comes that you cover the entire wound or the venom is, and then you treat the wound as best as you can.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the shoulder, belly, or intestine, and it is protruding, and you cover it, and it holds; and then cover the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then clean the wound as best as you can; and treat until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tines used to extract arrows is similar to the beak of a hedgehog, and it looks like this:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are different types: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the pointed hair is like the beak of a sparrow, to be inserted at the tip of the arrowhead, just as this is shaped:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the tines to be inserted and to be shaped is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of the veins that are safe to cut, there are XXXI, of which XVI are the largest, which is to say: the two that are after the ears, which are called the "herb" arteries; and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing; and the veins that are in the two lobes of the two eyes, which are called "aspirations"; and the vein that is cut in the front; and the vein that is cut at the top of the chin; and the guineas that are or col; and the veins that are in the lips of the mouth, which are called "augeherich" veins; and the veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	1. The veins that are commonly found in each arm are usually five: one is the cranial, which is on the left side of the costal, and it is called the "garden of the head" people; the other is called the fast, which is composed of the cranial and the basilar, and it is called the "garden of the chest"; and the basilar is if it is on the right costal, and it is called the "garden of the belly", and it is under the fascia, and it is the one that is found, which is open manifestly under the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	2. The saved vein is the one that is between the external and internal carotid arteries, and if it rains; and in the leg, there are three veins: one is the "garden of the gallbladder" which is on the left side of the costal, and the second one is the "gallbladder" which is at the ankle of the right costal; and the third one is called the "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other costal; and in the other leg, there are three veins like those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	1. The ear pains that follow the ears if aided by ancient cathaters and removers; and the quality of such healing, as I tell you, and it is that you raise the mouth of the patient, and wipe the ear with a rough cloth; then the patient's mouth is on a needle, as long as the ears appear behind the ears in the dependence of the chief: if you feel the pain in your own head, then it is good; then take the lancet, and cut through the vein just above the bone, then gently hold all the vein with both hands, and cover and the skin and the vein well enough to pass through, and make a sigh as you see; then tie and lie down, until it is healed as you see; then I have also said the incision and the cautery of the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	1. The health of the two arteries in the temples, if they are old, sore, and hardened, and have become accustomed to the watery humors; and if you judge it to be so, and the patient's pulse is weak, as the veins open widely; then you will feel the coldness of the hand, and then sign the index finger, and cut the lancet through, and lift the vein and the hand, as you have done in the other veins, and make the incision according to your necessity; then remove the reed, and put your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then form the wound, and leave it as long as it is sound; and we have spoken and of their extraction and of their removal, or at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The patient's face wound is as serious as the cranial wound, with ancient facial diseases, migraines, and bruising. If the physician suspects that the patient's collarbone is being pulled by the malaide as the wound opens, then they should take the instrument called the "fosseur", which looks like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then they should place the tip of the wound on the patient's hand or another part, and allow the blood to ooze out according to the amount you see; then they should cut the malaide's collarbone, and sew the wound as tightly as possible, never leaving an opening wider than a flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	All that is needed is for the flames to be just right; and the safe way, because it is close by, and by chance, the flames break when they are slightly touched.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The safety of the two veins that are in the linen sheets if they help, and the girdle, and the cut, and the orifice in the oil, and diseases of the face; and the quality of their safety if it is that the mallet twists the neck while twisting any line, as before; then the safe way, and so the safe way, a little long but wide flame a little large, because there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, by chance they are very sharp; then make quick bloodletting, as much as you can manage, and then tie the cloth, and hold it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	If the wound is clean and not too deep, and it is not gangrene, and not a disease of the face, as if it has bloody discharge, and becomes more painful with age; and the quality of the wound if the skin is tight around it, then tie the cloth around your left hand, and take a subtle flame and touch it to the corner of the lip that is between the two eyebrows, because the wound does not open very well, and it will now start to bleed; do not let it bleed too much, and make bloodletting according to your need, and then tie a cloth around it one night, because it will be quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The patient's health is aided in the relief of pain, and the onset of illness, and various diseases, and corrosions, and herpes, and empetigines; and the quality of the remedy if it is that the physician stretches his neck on both sides as we have said; and the physician being in the loyal service of the patient, and the patient sitting on the physician's knee, then cleanses the vein lengthwise widely, then draws out enough blood, as much as possible; then does another part in the other vein, then releases the line, and tightens and straightens the veins evenly so that the patient does not twist; and leaves it at morning, if the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the health of the deer
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the lips of the deer is helped to close in the mouth, and to prevent corruption of the genitals, and cracks of the lips, and sores and burns.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the health is to make the patient sit before you, and tighten his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the eyes, of which one is on the left side and the other on the right, and they are black due to their being dark, and because they have thin dark eyes: therefore, cut each one, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, then cut the largest of each part, and all the same way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the health of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The health of the tongue is affected by the health of the veins; if aid is given after the health of the head, and it is due to a sore throat, and diseases of the eyes, and diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the tongue is better when the patient's hands are in front of the sun and wets the tongue and looks at each side with a black vein: therefore both, and not too much, because these are arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The commonly affected veins are healthy in two ways: either by pressing on the entire flame with wide hands, or by using a fine olive oil as you would when trimming, and they are called "anesil"; and they are wide and fine according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the fire cautery is such that it is called a sword, and it is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	It has the skill to open the veins with flat hair-like stones that contain large clots and troubles; and this is the form of the fire cautery made of olive wood.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	It is more delicate to apply, and it is safer for the veins that are delicate, or if there is delicate clotted blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The salvation of the basilisk, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are caused by swelling of the throat, neck, belly, and other parts; and it is necessary for the healer to save wisely and avoid the artery that is swollen.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	If it pricks the artery, and blood comes out, then it must be stopped if possible; as I have said; and it should not be pinched by the fire, but cut if necessary.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	If the basculation does not open clearly, and you must pull it, and change another one; or you do not want any rain in it, or you want to draw out the vein from the arm: it opens clearly; and the fire is applied to the flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	If you see the vein of the healthy arm, and you must pull the arm, and touch the vein as far as you can see the pulse; then sign the vein is inflamed, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with the fire at the flame; and watch that you do not hurt the artery when you see the vein swell, because it is the artery: therefore shut it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. If you see flowing upwards like the urine of a child, and it is red and subtle, it is not from the artery: hurry to, and put your hand on it for a long time, then observe if it does not move; hold the shoulder with both hands, let it go, and do not move the member; and be careful, and do not move it until it is safe.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	2. And if it does not become inflamed, and it hurts, and the physician is not present, then if the artery has opened, because the head of the member has retreated; subside it.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	1. Take a scalpel from the fistula, and sharpen it, and take one of the halves and tie it well to the other; if it is not slippery, it is good; if not, then the treatment, as we have said, of the powders that make it slippery; the bindings are not easily moved in other positions for the small wound of the injury, and the pain of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	2. The health of the vein is improved if it is treated with the ointment that makes it slippery, and the pain of the chest, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic, as we have said; and it is necessary for the patient to rest the nerve that is in pain, and if it does not become too tight, and it relaxes the nerve, and it becomes gripped and healthy, and by chance it cannot be cured; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open any holes for its subtlety, then it is necessary that you heal the instrument's wound; and hide the nerve from your sight.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	If there is blood between the two veins, if they are long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The treatment of the head if it helps, that it attracts blood to the head and helps the wound; and it is better to help by touching with olive oil or sweet oil, because it is the most safe of all veins, because it does not harm the nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Indeed, it is better to touch it more lightly, and do not hurt the first time, and continue; and by chance, it inflames the wound in some men, but it does not hurt the first time.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about health is that it is to maintain good health and avoid diseases coming; and it should be made in one of the three veins: that is, the head, fast, and basilic; and it should be done at the beginning of each prayer, and during and after meals, when the sign of repletion appears; and it should be done the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The health that is maintained with diseases has no determination, but that when fasting it is of a day or night, in all hours and at any time; and it does not matter if the children are under 14 years old, or women who can only bear children after four months.

Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	When the patient is feeling better, if he has defecated, if he has not retained any feces, if the intestines are not superfluous and harmful to the members; nor if he is too fat or drunk, even if he has eaten too much, or been drugged; and if he becomes sicker after colic pain, vomiting, and abdominal discomfort, and many women give birth, and many women have labor pains, and many women have to urinate, and many women have to relieve themselves, and this is true for both men and women, and regardless of whether it is due to the arm or the chest; then subtly the humors are reduced, if he is not too large, by food and drinks and medicines, if you can afford it; then take a bath, nothing should displease you, to reduce the sweat, and make yourself healthy from the inside out, and through the third day, as we have said; and keep away from work, rest, luxury, and such things; and be modest and chaste, and be healthier than you are now, and rub your arms twice or three times with oil, then gently pull on the limb as much as it is tight or loose; and then rub the hands with oil, as long as the limbs are hot, and feel them; then dry the patient with a little oil, then put his hand in his left hand on the place where the wound was, if the wound is not healed, and it does not hurt, then dip his hand in oil, and press it on the wound as much as it hurts the limb; and if the wound is healed, do not touch it with your hand.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that run like cords to the healthier parts, and if they are many, then when one is placed on the fire, it retreats from the fire, and cannot open the vein, and then it is one of those; and if the vein is closed, it is the wound too tight, for then it comes to the healthier parts, and the healthier parts must be advised in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez. Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	2. If several abscesses occur repeatedly, once it is healthy and the vein opening is small, if you hurry, and soak a soft sponge in cool water and wring it out, and stretch it for an hour; and it is necessary to do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if there is no black or green matter at the site of the vein after several days, if you don't know; and if you see, put nothing of aloe or remedy in water of calamine, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	2. Many times abscesses and inflammation occur at the health of the church: therefore put your hand there, and if that appearance is painful, compress the hand with the leu.

The patient should not place anything else on the body as we have said, for fear of cutting the artery; but I applied a dry cloth to endure the pain, then another treatment, until it is healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to its quantity and color of the serum.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it drain as long as it is red; and if you see a large amount, let it drain as much as it becomes thin; and if it is too cold, let it be cooled down.
