And it has two palm-wide and half a palm in width, and has a small pertussis on one side, like a needle, and is of iron or steel, so that it does not pierce the patient's skin; and in the middle, there is a wire of iron or steel, to insert a cord, and in this there are large and small loops according to the diseases and weight of those who take them, because the cautery of children are different from those of adults, and the thin ones are different from the fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	1. And it must be put on the wound above the member: take the candle or liniment, and put it at the end of the wound where the wound is, so that it does not burn the patient; then put it on the member, and you must put it on the sutures that we have said, if you see, if there is vapor coming out, and then remove the wound; and take the liniment as before, and repeat it often, if you can.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	1. In the wound that is in a patient with a cold, there is no gauze or pustules, and it is not infected unless it is only when it is clear of fever, and it is placed on the member only then; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	1. Withouts are not taken except in parts where it is possible to put splints due to their small size, like the lips and genitals, and similar parts; and in these parts, if they are naked of char, like doves or needles, and other similar parts; and the quality of the user is that when you find withouts which are in soft waters, if you take them; you put a nut in soft water, as long as they are free of any children, and have no vomiting; then it is healthy for the vein and the wound, then wash the member as much as it is red, and put on the withouts; and when they are smooth, and cherish, if it is the lower part or the upper, if it can be put on with a ventouse, then it is good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If the wound is not clean, then lift the limb, and then the swelling; and if the patient's arm is too tight after the wound, then use a cold flax bandage, and apply it as long as the swelling remains; and if the swelling increases, then use a mixture of vinegar or galls, and similar things, until it is reduced; or you can use half a dozen peeled onions and leave them on the limb as long as they burn, so that it will now be anesthetized; and if you have more wounds, then use other onions.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not take on the salve, then cleanse the lesion with fresh salve or thread as much as it will hold, and then insert them, and as they feel the salve, if they burn; and when you see that they are healing, apply a little aloe and linen, or smoke, if they now cherish.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and they are the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Explain to me, what the folk say of this book, that they have never seen any of the ancient books, nor any letters; and for this reason, the science has been neglected in our land, because I have never found any boast; and I do not know if there is any, except that through the science of the old books, or because I have studied so much and treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described in this book what is contained in it, and I have summarized at the end, and I have clearly shown the shapes of the fractures that have been broken, as I have done in these two books before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say at the beginning of this book the sum of the words and chapters or sentences where one's understanding meets, and more so if those who have experienced it understand and learn this noble art, and learn to teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, or twist, or tortuousness occurs in no part of the body, if nothing can be done to help the patient on one side and the other, whether it is due to weakness, or young age, or feebleness; or if the patient is not very thin, or too fat; and if the patient is too thin, that means cold joints, and thin bones, and does not drink any wine, nor eat thin grasses, and does not fill the veins with blood, until there is no doubt of apoplexy, or expansion of matter in the member; if the patient recovers after the first government used by him.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the bones begin to heal, if it is necessary to remove the patient's flesh that causes great swelling, or if there is viscosity, like dough when cooked in boiling water, and testes, and pies, and pancakes of wool, and cheese, and fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the more the swelling is reduced, the fracture heals faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And you advise that broken bones and deformities cannot be well repaired or corrected according to their nature by the hands of the members, nor as those that are too flexible; but if it is possible, reset the broken bone with large tendons that are sutured and joined together as much as possible, just as it was before; and do not cut it off completely, and for this reason it is necessary to remove large amounts of flesh, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you know that fractures come in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the skull is different from that of the arm or leg, and I will tell you all the kinds of fractures in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another that breaks when struck, like the size of a quill to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a small notch.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each fracture has its own way and tool in restoration, according to what remembrance comes to the patient's mind; and the fracture of the bone is by what part it appears to be torn, and open well by defense, and some pressure of the hand; and if it is not tortuosity, and pain is not felt in the wound, and there is no fracture, then there is no tortuosity, or notch, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you can only manage to move it with your hand, but take the medicine that comes afterward, and then try again gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And you should be concerned about the fracture that will occur in the bone, and the two parts that are separated. Now you should aim to put them back in place as evenly as possible, without causing further pain; if the pain subsides, then leave it alone until the swelling is reduced. Then gently and carefully put it back in place, and be assured that the restoration of this bone will be lighter than the restorations of other bones with pieces missing. Then try again gently.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	1. And if there are broken pieces in the bone of the foot, if they are two parts, it is hands or fingers, or a part of your finger, or a cord, or a cord and your hand; and place the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are adjusted, if you reset by your effort the additions in their place in the muscle that you see, and keep that by your effort does not cause the surgeon's injury or pain; and adjust well the two ends of the bone in the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	2. And if it seems to you that it is not well, if it curves beautifully and does not strain too much, do not press as those who come by their own effort cause the member to contract and draw tight, as we have often wanted.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	When the member is painful, if the patient carefully instructs the shoulder not to move at all, neither by day nor by night, neither by turning nor in any other way; and it is well that the member feels secure so that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it does not feel any pain, if it is not dislocated, and it is necessary to put it in proper position so that it does not feel any pain; and you keep it steady until it is restored, and the quality of the broken member is according to what I am saying.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	It is said that the broken member has different sizes in smallness and greatness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	1. For it has bitten off limbs, just as if they were wheat and straw: if it comes to wrapping them in linen cloths and bandages; and the large ones, like sticks and stems: if it comes to wrapping them in a wide and hard piece of linen, for the large limbs embrace all the great member, and draw it evenly, so that there is no part left untied, then the small pieces are lightly tied with three or four turns around the member, and the hand is tightly tied to each part of the limb, then go to the end of the fracture and tighten it less than the fracture allows, until the fracture is sufficiently softened to a great part of the healthy part, then take another piece of linen and turn it back on the other side of the fracture, then return to the part opposite the fracture, and tighten it gently, not too tight nor too loose, as we have said in the first part of the fracture; then put between the wrapped limbs of linen or bandages, as they are equal, and then put all of them on, and then put your well-made ties on, if it has not caused an apoplexy or hematoma.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if it is inflamed or gangrenous, then put on something soothing for gangrene, which helps to reduce inflammation and leave no marks; then tightly tie your eyes, and they should be of a width equal to one wide, well-shaped catchet, or of rings made from palm fronds, or of bands of palm leaves, and they should be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the one you put on the wound be larger and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as the member is small or large; then tie the eyes in the same way as before, then put a thread around it, as was done in the first loop; the more it is stretched, the less; and the thread must be even, neither too thick nor too thin, and should be of linen; for if the thread is too thick, like the works of fools who make their laces with linen threads, it is a great error, for the loop cannot be even if it is too fine, and it only serves to make each eye smaller and less spaced.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is dislocated by the shoulders after the stripping of the arms in healthy ones, then they must put on the threads of linen or silk, if it does not bend.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splint, and the edge is broken, I will tell you the treatment for this afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And it is said that it is not easy to straighten all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not easy to straighten them on the first day; and according to your skill in amputation, after five or seven days, or more, depending on the severity of the injury; and the old way of restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsion: and that you take flour that is between the bolts of the mill, and knead it with a great deal of yeast, and make this dough, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of restoring fractures in other positions, as well as for women and children, because it is not too hard or too soft.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	1. Another way to mend breaks and dislocations and twists: take barley, lard, and umber, and Arabic gum and mugate, in the ratio of X to V; aloes and VIIII, and made into powder, and mixed with wool of ox dung; if the complexion of the face is hot, it can be used as this plaster, because it has a good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	1. Another way to mend twists: take Arabic gum and vinegar, in the ratio of X to VIIII; aloes and VI, and arsenic, and mix well, and cook with water or ox dung, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Other ways to make a plaster for joints and bones, and alleviate the pain coming, and the size uses of the bone, and the fracture: take new flour, and the dough melted with oil and cooked, and put on the leg.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Other plasters do not cure, but they are useful for alleviating post-operative pain and proper bone pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Other ways to make a plaster that cures broken bones: take dry fig leaves and earth pottery and boil together, and make the plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Other ways to make a plaster for bone fracture repair and to relieve post-operative pain.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	The root of vismvle, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of wheat, of each a part; and boil, and conserve with wine, and the members are soaked, and it is conserved with fresh coriander water, or with water, and it is used.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to apply more force than the first, when the abscess is deeply located, comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Boil the roots of vismvle, and linseed meal, balsam, honey, and salt, and violet and chamomile flowers, of each a part; and boil, and conserve with fresh salty water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the choler of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras says in his book that no one puts on the broken limb to restore it as if it were made of wax and oil, and nothing more, and he says that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It seems that Galen says that things like hot wax and oils, such as myrrh and frankincense, and similar things, should be used to restore the broken limb, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat wounds and pain: take a piece of cloth and thread it with the hairs of an ox or the feathers of a goose, or silk, and sew, and stitch, and apply it to the wound, and then cover it with a piece of cloth.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the wound gradually heals, and the patient feels no pain in the bone of the limb; if it does not heal by hand pressure, and pain or pruritus comes to the bone, if you haste, and remove it, and now apply the plaster; then gently drape, and wet the sea sponge, and dip in cold water, and raise the limb as much as the pruritus ceases and the pain subsides; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry cloth, moisten with cold or rose oil, and tie with a bandage, as long as you are sure not to have post-operative shock; and allow the inflammation in the member to subside, and the pain to subside, then resume gentle application of the plaster, a little emplaustre, and do not strain it too much; and gradually as it heals.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is painful and inflamed and swollen, and it recurs, as you have done previously, if you follow the treatment.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if you do not see any sign of improvement within three days or four or seven, and never more than twenty days, as soon as the wound begins to heal and approaches the bone, then increase the restraint more than before, and the flesh will grow larger, just as I have said before; and if you see the skin becoming drier than it should be, apply warm poultices every time you remove the bandage, and once a day, and cut off the norrissemens at the joint; in this way you will cure the norrissemens at the joint, and stop the inflammation that causes the limb to ache: this is harmful, and if it does not improve within a week, I know of no other remedy than to apply ointment and keep the bandage on straight.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various kinds of wounds
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of wounds, and various forms, and the causes are assigned; for there are wounds made by the blow of a spear, and the whole bone is cut off that is the bone, if it is broken like a knife or a fork; and therefore this kind of wound is called "cut" or "hack".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	The spear cuts the bone by one sense of feeling and is called this kind of wound "absolute"; and it is the wound of these two great or small wounds.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is a blow that is embedded, or a cut or a cut of the bone, or a piercing under the bone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If there is a persistent fracture, which approaches the tissue that is loose from the bone, or it is against the bone, and this wound or large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	If there is a healed wound that is as subtle as a cut, and it is a small fracture, and for this it is called the "capillary" fracture; and if the wound is made by hurting with a pierce, or with a nail, or with something else, and it lets the piece of the bone enter, and it is the same size as when they healed the burns; if it enters through the piercing.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	When the bones are wet, such as in the case of children, and they break in various ways, those that are lighter are more broken than others; and I will speak about this in their language.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of fractures by the force that causes them, and by the tests they have undergone, and by the corrupted cartilage that is present.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The visible appearance is known by the fact that when the bone is discovered and the edges are rubbed, if the dark fracture is not open, it is not considered a true fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, be careful with the patient's condition, and if you see no serious accidents, such as vomiting, understanding, extension, and swelling, fever, and the wounds turning red and becoming more inflamed, and other similar signs that cannot be cured with doubt, then you must consider it a true fracture.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see an unexpected accident, and you hope for a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the first bone comes to you, and it is in the hand, then it is necessary to cut the bone before the fourth year of life.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is in this way, then if you cut the bone before the ninth year of life, then the bone will not be cut correctly, and the accident that we have mentioned will come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	If the bone fracture comes near the edge of the bone, then if you cut the bone in this way, then you should cut off the broken part: and it is that you pull the head of the new bone, and cut through the bone in all the ways that you can, and cut the shape of the wound as large as you can, and it comes to reveal the bone, or the bone is broken, and if it helps to do this, and it is that you fill the joint with smooth oily powder; and then rest the wound until the broken bone is calmed and secured against displacement; then begin to cut the bone, and it is done according to two ways of carving: one way is that you cut at the narrowed end, and it is in this form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I cut another one that is larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is if you have many different sizes, some narrow and others wide, and they are sharp, and they are made of iron; and you work them lightly so as not to cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and brittle, it comes to pass that you perforate it, otherwise you should maintain the size with needles, and do not make them too large or too small, so that they do not pass over the bone; and you must have more, so that each one fits well in its joint of the bone, if you have needles for each test; and this is the form of the three ways of needles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	1. The quality to perceive through the broken bone is that you place ice on the bone, and turn it around until you feel that the bone is perceived; then put the ice back another part a little later, and then do everything, then cut the incisions in the bone that is between the points, and do it as subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, as you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the trumpets that you have like needles, pincers; and make sure you do not touch the scalp or the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have perceived and treated the bone, if it covers that the tool that is made of the bone is made to another instrument resembling an incision, but it should be more narrow and subtle than the other incision; and if it does not make any small bones, nor any scales, if the light bones are gently in the trumpets; then cure the wound with tentions and dressings that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of opening is when it is done by the Gaulish method, which is more skilled; and the large incision, and that is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to remove a part of the bone, where the open fracture is visible, so that once you have removed this part, you can measure from the top of this incision, and its form will be:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut too much, and the part that is cut is towards the bone; then firmly hold a small tool, so that you lightly touch the entire bone, and be well prepared for the cloth that is on it; if it is near the bone, if the bone is light, because it is easy to handle, and causes pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not pierce the skin, and the bone is only covered by soft tissue, and it has small pieces, then cover those sharp edges with something, and smooth out the scales with a subtle rasp, as you must have various quantities of it to serve each limb according to the type and appearance of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you use a coarse rasp first, and then a softer one, and continue to do this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In every other hair removal and fine fracture, you must serve according to its address; and this is something that cannot be repeated for the one who has studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	1. If the wound is discovered, it comes to pass that you should first apply linen to the wound, according to the size of the wound, and grease it with olive oil, and place it over the wound; then take another doubling of linen, either II or III, and grease it with wine and olive oil, and place it over the first linen; and do this more gently than you would, so that you do not burn the smoke, then dress with other linen, and do not strain it too much, only as much as it covers the wound, and leave it for I jor or II, until the inflammation is calmed, then remove it, and administer medicines as follows: roots of lis, flour of times, powder of incense, aristolochum, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and place it over the wound, and administer further medicines without burning; and be sure that the wound is clean, so that you do not leave any ointment or bandage on it, for if a bandage is placed on the bare skin, it can cause great harm to the patient, as it can irritate the skin and cause pain. For if you apply something greasy to the wound, it will cause pain to the patient.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	1. Prepare well, as there is no need for accidents to happen to the patient, just as we have said, if it is doubtful, then so be it.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	2. And if nothing comes out but the medicine we have put in, then part of honey and three parts of rose oil and one part of glue, and let it be applied to the face; then the cure is done in ways that suit the patient's condition, as long as they are healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	3. It is said that the two parts of bone and joint are never broken, or only one, because they are two bones; and this is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it is twisted or bent, and then it becomes healthy.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	If one of the two parts is broken, then if you can reach your small toe or finger tip, and make the break even with your index finger, and in the pocket as long as it does not deviate from its natural figure; and do this lightly, and tell the patient that the helper does not feel pain through their shoulder.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the break is in the part of the finger, and cannot reach the shoulder, then if you can put it even at the head of a large pocket,
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If the break is in the other part, then if you redo it and wait to restore the first joint, if possible; otherwise, after the ninth or tenth day, when the swelling has subsided, then reach for the tip of the finger with your thumb, if the break is in a part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	1. If you cut at another part, it will be; and the wounds should be so large that they fill the cavities with blood.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	2. And no restorer will say that you must smooth the wounds in the burr, and each day will die.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	3. It seems to me that it is only right, but the wounds should be smoothed in the making of a bun of horse dung and powdered milled flint; then leave the wound, as long as the bone is firm, and the cartilages harden.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	4. And never cut on the neck of the wound, and if it is too loose, and holds the breastplate, and blows the salves among; or do as you have seen.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if the abscess ruptures, come to the physician as soon as you can, for it may be that he puts on a piece of cloth or a piece of silk dipped in rose oil, or in a drop of vinegar.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess does not come, then put on ointment made of flour and powdered incense, mixed with eggs, and then put on light bandages, and do not close the wound; and if the wound in the nose is small, and it is torn into small pieces, then if there are suitable stitches available for this, then sew them, and treat the scar as best as possible, and make it look like the rest of the skin; and if there is no plague on the wound, then treat it with poultices and bandages, and put on charred twigs, until it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the dislocation of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is dislocated, there is no wound, and the fracture is slight only, and not broken into pieces, but rather cracked like a shell, if you understand, lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the left part, to place your index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, then place your index finger on the right hand, lightly touch the fracture, and feel for the other hand, and hold it steady.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the lower jaw is divided into two parts, then it comes to administer an extension of two parts, as long as it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth move or fracture, or if they are pulled by a gold or silver or silk thread, then place them on the broken lower jawbone, and place one double drapery; and place one double stitch well made, or a piece of leather even, long and wide according to the size of the jawbone, and tie it to the cheek that you use, and command the patient to lie down, and give light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	1. If you see that the joint changes shape, if it is left to itself, and then reset to its original position; and apply a plaster with flour from the miller's mill, or wheat flour, after you have washed the skin; and apply a light plaster, and let it dry, and the joint's shape does not change, leave it as it is, until it is healthy; it becomes healthy many times in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	2. And if the plaster comes off, if you do not follow what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	3. And if there is a fracture and wound together, remove a small piece of bone from the joint; if the bone has flexible bones, it can be bent.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is wide, let it be cleaned according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have all these pieces, and there is no need for anything else, if the wound is wide, make sure it is clean, and then insert some adhesive bandages to support the plaster, until it is healthy.
de la forcele	of its strength.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks more often in front of the shoulder, towards the elbow, and the break is in three ways: it is broken and separated into two, with two pieces, and it is lighter to restore; or it is broken with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	1. And the operation is done when the fracture is sensed as a wound, if you have two assistants, that one of them examines the helper who feels the force of the fracture; and the other extends the collar towards the part, then place the fracture equally in your two hands, if it forms as it should, and there should be no appearance or change.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	2. And if you are more skilled at extending, if you put the shoulder blade against the patient's back, with a round or oval bead of linen or wool, according to your need; and you make it lighter and draw the bead to your hand, so that you place the fracture equally in both hands, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you do not treat the head of the strong force immediately, because it comes from afar, then the patient's pain will increase, and they should loosen the shoulder and earlobe, and pull the muscles of the shoulder away, as long as the bone of the strong force is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture to your two sides, and if you cannot hold the fragments together, then cut them loose; and take out the lighter pieces, and if the bone does not join by any means to any part of the incision that you made, but put the strong force instrument away for safety:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	The text seems to describe a situation where a spoon appears, is not very sharp, and should be as wide as the limb desires, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the will; if there are two heads, as you see, and some are wide, and others are thin, as the swelling of the wound you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of a cut, if the wound is large, or if it is small, if you doubt a cut, then use dressings of linen and bandages, according to their quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if you cut yourself, if it is large, then use oil of rose and essence and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	1. The healing of the bone, when it feels pain and discomfort, is to put the powdered sulfur and wool of urine on the bone, and lightly sprinkle some salt on it, and then place a small thick branch of palm leaves, and gently wrap around the bones; then take a fine wire of three to four inches long and long, and wrap it around the branch, and tie it; then take a subtle wire of three to four inches long and long, and wrap it around the branch, and make sure the bend of the branch is tight; then place the wire under the bend, so that the end of the bend is tight; and place the wire on the brace, and turn the bend under the collar, and loosen the saddle; and pull out the wire from each part, and when you see that the brace holds the brace firmly, and you see clearly that the wire does not move away from the bone breakage, each reward a certain amount, and when the mallet is loose, and if the mallet is tight; and make the mallet on its back, and put it when it falls a small pillow of the saddle, for raising the mallet to the top; if you can straighten the bone breakage by straightening the shoulder or by pulling the arm to the collar, and if it does not slip accidentally, in about twenty days; then resume the wrapping, if you see that it is suitable, and hold and release it as soon as it is restored; and it is restored in about twenty-eight days, and less in no man.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the injury to the elbow
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement. de la brisure dou pis	of the break
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is never broken in its environment, but this sometimes happens; but it often breaks in the defense.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the field, if it is not aligned properly, and great pain is felt, and lack of strength, and all, and by chance vomiting blood, and the wounds are opened in the broken bones, and it feels well.

If the dislocation is on the shoulder and the patient cannot move it, place a bandage between the spines, press the spines, assemble the costal cartilages at your hands, subtly put them equal to all ways you can until the bone looks as it should; then put on plasters and poultices of salt or another light substance, wrap it in a cloth, and tie it around the broken bone so it doesn't move; and turn the ligament back on itself, tighten it gradually, and reward each hour if it holds, and if it loosens, if it's due to corrosion or pruritus that comes to the shoulder, or pain or apoplexy, if you haste, and it slips, and remove the bandage, and address what came from the ways of cures; then rebandage it, and tighten it as much as it is healthy.
de la brisure des costes	Of the breast wound
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois. de la brisure dou col	Of the break of the shoulder
