de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the upper and lower "femur," where one is larger and the other is smaller, and by chance, only the large femur or the smaller one is broken, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light and the healing; and when the large bones are broken, if it is a poor healing and more lame than when they were broken individually.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bones that are broken, then it will be necessary to lightly extend and put them even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bones, then they must be more tightly strained; and stretch it over the thumb, and lift the palm of the hand higher than the others, and the legs below them lower than the others, and let the marrow press against itself, and the thumb higher, so that the marrow suffers no labor; then stretch the muscles of the arm to the part opposite the shoulder, or to the elbow, and some other muscles to the other side.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then he places the head evenly, according to its better form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, then he puts each in its place, and if there are no loose ends that point out the joint, and you cannot restore it to its place, then as we have said before, set it and the bone.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the break there is a wound, then I have spoken to the individual chirurgeon; if they take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of the restoration there are gangrene wounds, then make a drapery of oil of rose and blennik candle, which is neither too hard nor too soft, and wrap it around subtly as long as the gangrene wounds are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then the bone, and he puts the powder of the mill with a lot of urine, puts the seeds, and makes the briseure further apart, and a little wider than the others; and checks that it has VI briseures or braces in more positions: whether it is the briseure in one of the bones, or in II; and is drawn more under the briseure than other parts, and fewer by moving away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and are the seeds that are under the briseure wet and moist, and not too hard or sharp; and is the filth, which is extracted, of lin, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the limb after some time.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any accidents come to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, if you cool the member with warm water as long as the itching is relieved; and let the member rest undisturbed.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then the swelling resumes, and if the limb is softened and the bones are destroyed, and it seems like something, it should be treated.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the knife-wounds cannot come to the member because it is too tight, such that you soften it in a poultice, and let it rest for some time until the wounds are closed and then draw it out.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things come to the patient, within twenty years.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If the shoulder is dislocated, then the patient can move their hands to their collarbone, and it should be even; and they should rest and be still, and sleep on their back; and it is hoped that this dislocation is restored in thirty years or thirty-five, and by chance in twenty years, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Wishes that on the back of the hand and in the two wrists there are few dislocations, and only painful ones, and not many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	When the bone of the hand is broken or crushed, and it is broken, and it lies straight in front of him; then he places his hand on the extended nail, and extends the fingers of the broken bones, and places them evenly in the holes, as they are well joined; then he applies plaster and bandages, if necessary, and puts a splint according to the quantity of the nail; and it is wrapped in a curve like linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is at the heel of the plant, then I make a spool of linen, and command the patient to pull on his broken heel; and then he pulls on a long spool, and it should be the splint as large as the sole of the foot, and it is pulled, if it can be done.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the shoulder, then it comes to pass that you place a splint on it, and another in the foot, if the hand is over-bent and straight, then the arm is completely fixed, and the limb is placed between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture does not occur in both arms, but is in one, and it is placed correctly, then as it should be; and the hand is pulled up with the foot, and you see if a splint is placed right on the fracture, and it does not move; and if the fracture is in other parts, such as the index finger or one of the others, and it is placed correctly, and the hand is held in place with the healthy finger that follows; or you tie them all together, whatever you can, or you place a splint on it, as I have said; and be careful in the restoration and the position of the wound closure, and see what comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken branch
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the branch is often broken in two places, and it can be seen when it turns forward and backward; if the restoration is successful, it depends on whether the bones on either side of the break are united or not.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient feels pain in their face, and then extends each muscle in their limb according to their ability; and it is when the break is complete that the bone is set.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the branch, then some of the fibers may be towards the point of the arrow, and the others away from the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And as it has reached the joint, and then release the ligaments of the joint, and extend the limb; then place the bone even with your two hands, according to its natural figure, and then insert the splint, and the bandage, if it does not move.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if it has been strained, if you let it rest, then return to your work and your care; the bandage is made in a partial manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the ankle with a bandage doubled in length from I to II or III, and remove any excess, then bend the leg until the heel reaches the root of the nail, and tie the long end of the bandage between the knee and the leg, releasing the joint of the knee; then wrap around the leg and the knee the bandage, then put on the bracelets, and place an estile on the bone of the leg; then place the leather between the leg and the knee to fix the splint, then start tying form III or IV on the bracelet; and as more bracelets you put on, less the leg is tightened; then take out the two ends of the thread that you have tied between the leg and the knee, and on the three estiles that are placed, then return to the knee at the chief of the thread, until you see the patella; the splint, if it does not move from its place, then let it be, then k'il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it happens, if it is not treated, and he addresses what comes, as we have said many times; and if it has pieces of bone that prick, if it can be managed, then it can; and if it cannot, then it can be cut and drained, and the cure as we have said, depending on how healthy it is.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never has the joint been broken unless it is set by oneself or the other arm; however, in the restoration that is made, it does not cause pain to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And you should know that the joint is restored in L hours, or less or more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	Of the ruler's great pain
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	It is said that in the ruler's great pain, there is only slight breakage, but it pulsates many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, if not but a scratch, or a puncture, and comes to all wounds, and feels pain, and that is well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when you put back what has been lost in its place as much as possible, and then apply the plaster, and put a round stitch, if you can, and draw it tight, and pull it as it should be, and reward all the dispositions we have said for other fractures, such as apoplexy and other similar ones; and if you do the same for each accident, as much as possible, and make it healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	It is said that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called on the right side "canine" and the other is called "fox-like," and they are both equally brittle as in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is done in the same way as the arm. And if the two bones are broken at once, then turn the leg from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, turn forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bones are broken, if it hurts much and you see well, then turn around.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Adonques, ensure proper extension and place it evenly; however, it is necessary to check if the fracture is stable, and if there are more pieces, then the extension should be smaller and lighter; and align according to your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your operation, if you find two strips of wool that are pricking the leg on one side and the other, and are long enough from the knee to the ankle, then wrap them around the leg and tie them at both ends, and lay them along the limb, and do not let the leg shift to the right or left, and it is well; and no one has caused pain in the leg, and it was made of fist, and I put it on the leg to warn against movement, and properly done, it is made in the fracture or wound; and shake each time the leg to see if there is any swelling or other accident; if the cure is as soon as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the breaking of the bones of the hand
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is never a break, but the bones of the hand are never broken and must be careful not to twist in more positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones of the hand are broken and you see these bones sticking out of each other, if they are so sore on the earth, just like when you were flying, then now put your hand on the side, lift the bone as much as it can be, then press it until it seems to be in its place; then put the splint and sew up the wound at the end of the thumb, then draw the cloth around the thumb, and other things that you have skill for.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if the joint does not move, because you will find the bones even, they may be broken, they may be dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the two broken, if they are repaired, as we have said, then put a splint on one of them according to the length of the other; and make a larger pouch for it, then put the pulley that I mentioned in place, and draw it gently; and if there are II or III, or more, broken, then put one on each according to its quantity, wrapped in one layer of linen, and draw the pulley away from the point of the bone; and make sure it is held steady while the belly of the point is pressed against the abdomen of the bone, so that it is well sanded.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not overlook the other things I have said about other fractures, as soon as we have said them; and treat each accident as we have suggested.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone point
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the woman's bone is broken, if it is set in place, then it leans towards the side of the shoulder, and is held by the hand; then fill the nature of the wound with cloth, and put it on as much as possible; then bend the woman, and gently raise the shoulder a little at a time, until the cloth comes into the nature, and the bone returns with the stitch; and when she sees that the cloth is wet, if the bone is wet, and when she has passed it, put it back in place, and make seven turns or turns: if the fracture is restored, and you see it, take a basin of wine, and tie it to the arm with a string, and blow all the wine into the nature; then form the clot in the arm, as long as the wine is drawn out: the nature will return to the fracture; then fill it with cloth, and leave it alone for several days, until it is healthy.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	When the bone of the elbow is broken, or of the woman, if it is repaired as we have said in the elbow of the horse; and these breaks are not hidden that are near to him who puts his study and his use, and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break indicates in more ways the right way of restoration: understand the direction.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the limb, when it is broken, take an ostrich gullet and pull the bone; then wrap with cloths, and leave it three turns or more outside, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a wound with pain, even if it is large, to have it treated immediately, just as the bone of the arm or shoulder, or similar, so that it becomes healthy now, since the wounds we have spoken of testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the healthy wound is scarred, if you have nothing else, then continue to restore the break at the same time tomorrow, or the next day, if you are not able to come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if you are not able to come the next day, then leave the restoration for the following day, as long as you are calmed, and do not touch it again on the third or fourth day, because you will make the unpleasant accident worse.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks, it is exposed due to the knee discovered, so it comes that you put it lightly in your hands, at a slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not fit to put evenly in your hands, so if the clamp has this instrument which is of iron, which is VII or VIII in length, and the width is according to the size of the wound; and for this it is a matter of the shoulder that he grasps three or four, according to how much he has experience in each treatment of fracture; and it should be strong and a bit large, so that it does not slip at the compression of the member on your hand, and also in front, and large before, in this way:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And is called "palisade", because it requires that the heads of the bones be placed on the head of the bone; and the bore once, as it rises, and it should be even between the two.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is hidden, and the fragments cannot well grasp the bone, then it comes that you cover the head of the bone with something, as long as the fragments are in their place.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you do not reset the bone, as we have said, if it is covered with an instrument that is suitable for this, or sharp or pointed, then you should reinsert the part that has been removed from the bone with roughness and small particles.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	When the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, one should suspect that something is wrong with its natural state.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you continue until it is in its proper place, then dress the wound with a piece of black vinegar cloth, and do not put anything else on it, such as oil or grease, otherwise it will cause putrefaction and corruption; then apply ointments to the bone after resetting it, leave the wound open, and cover it with a dressing according to the size of the wound, and be careful not to tighten the wound with the fracture; often they have had this result, and have caused the patient to die or corrode never; and the stripes become more slick and slippery than the other scars.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	When the wound is large or great, and you doubt that it will come out, as we have said, and you feel pain in the leg, but it cannot be set with nails; but envelopes instead, in the leg of the nails, strengthen hard threads, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	When you see after the first or second day, if the bone is not fixed, and it has moved all around, and you have applied an ointment to heal the wound, if a medicinal ointment and similar things are used.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	It is necessary that you stretch the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is not too tight and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	It is necessary that the limbs are aligned in a way that the belly is not affected lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If they persist, and the belly cannot be held back, but rather moves towards the belly, with small pieces of bones, because it is necessary that the wound is covered with tent, and all these broken pieces cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	If an abscess comes to the limb, or any other form of corruption, and you must treat it according to what is written in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	If the bone is broken and exposed through the limb, as if it were the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar bones of the large limbs, if you do not treat it, because often death comes several times, but leave it until it has bled; by chance, it may heal after 20 days or 30, and treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Of the burns that come from the heat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We come often after the hardening of the bone, but when it is near the joint, and it is a shame to see the limb in such a position; and by chance, it cannot make the limb its natural shape.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the wound is fresh: if it is treated with stupefying drugs, such as aloe, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, and other similar things, either none of these, or all together, and mix them with warm stupefying wine or with a large amount of beer or vinegar; and put them in the mouth, and draw it well, and do not let it drip from the hands; and then draw it out, and resume another one, as long as the necrotic tissue is healed; or if you strain a piece of splint well made; for the property of the splint is that it holds all the tendons in place on the limbs; and if the necrosis has already turned into hardness, and is like a piercing, and it is bleeding from the socket, and the cope is set, and makes the apparent superfluity disappear; or if you cut it off completely, as long as it is healed, and the cure as soon as it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	a limb that is weak after a struggle
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and weakens after the weak limbs and subtle, if it comes from causes: either because one was too tightly bound, and was not well-bound; or because it had too many ligaments, and could not come to the member; or for a multitude of inflammation; or for too great movements, not in its time; or because it has little blood in its body, and is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And if the cure is that you make the patient drink warm water, and make the body tense as much as possible without multiplying in it; then give him cold baths, and joy and relief; then apply poultices to the limb, if it attracts the great inflammation, and the swelling often becomes acute until the inflammation reaches the member; and then he returns to his natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The dislocated limb after the injury.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is swollen after the restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the dislocated form of the limb is deformed, it is not its natural state: if one does not believe the fools who say that the whole bone must be broken at once, and all the others have done this in our land; and these bones are blamed, and great harm comes to them, and by chance they die; however, if the wounds and tortures are fresh, and it is necessary to heat them with hot water, or herbs that soften, if like cabbage, and roots, and honey-suckle, and similar things; and I apply a mollifying ointment, as well as dysentery is made, and I take the mucilage of cabbage, and cook it with lard or olive oil, and apply it on; or I take fat figs, and roast them with fat, and similar medicines that dry the sweat.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And no time is there where the nodation is not continued and long with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be movement in the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is aroused and becomes painful, like a wound, and there is need for the oyster to be heated, if it comes close to the bone, by subtle and light incision; and then put on and studied in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs at no joint, if it comes now to bring sense to the target.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if we delay, if it swells, and by chance if we reset it on the shoulder; because then we cannot move it to the ear where it is swollen: many times come spasm and other pains; always, when this happens, I make the patient healthier, then let him, as long as the abscess is pained, then anoint the member with hot oil and ointment, then reset it gently, and cure each member as we do in its own shoulder.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the treatises for the dislocations of the shoulder bones.
des mandibules	for the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	There are times when the mandibles are dislocated, and the dislocations of both sides are in two ways: either they are a small piece of their bones, and are softened slightly; or they are completely dislocated, and hang downwards, and cut off the saliva from the mouth that they cannot hold, and cannot close their mouth, and wrap around their tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	If the dislocation is small, it returns through the more frequent positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And when it is complete and accomplished, if you reset it as soon as possible, and do not force it; in such a way that the patient's hand leaves the injured person's head, and marks the root of the dislocation of the mandible, which causes the dislocation to be of the second part; and the other two hands are deformed, to make them equal; and command the injured person to smooth and move their jaws, and all parts.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the patient places it evenly, as it should be in its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is reset gently, at the same time, it is the second mandibles that are assembled, as long as the hands are oiled and warm, but do not force it; and do not force it as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	When they are properly realigned and the patient's mouth feels relaxed, if it is wrapped with soft cloths made of oil of rose and wax, then lightly tie the eyes with threads; the patient should sleep on their back, and their head should be between two pillows, so that they do not move to the right or left, nor strain themselves, but gently eat lean meat, as long as the pain is steady and does not affect the jaws; then take what they see lightly, and do not try to open the mouth with their teeth and drink, as long as the jaw is well soothed and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be set at once in an hour and are not converted to their proper position, if fever and sickness are usual, and by chance the abdomen becomes distended, and by chance vomiting is of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	When you see this, you will know it is a disaster; many have died in nine years.
de la forcelle	of force.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The force cannot be removed by the cost of the continuation of the hand and the foot, and it is never set free at the end, but it is felt to be so.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is when the patient grows sick on his back and extends his arms; then press the palm of your hand against the cheek, it will return; then place the plaster and bandage over it, and draw it tight; and the part that is towards the shoulder cannot be set free; if not, and if it is never free, then reset it at the shoulder, as we have said; then place the plaster and bandage over it, and draw it tight, and command the patient to rest as soon as he is healthy; and then you bring back the head of the shoulder when it is dislocated from its socket.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways in which the shoulder dislocates: either it dislocates at the head of the bone, or at the top of the shoulder; or it dislocates at the side, and this happens rarely; or it dislocates at the back, and this is more common, and does not dislocate the elbow, because at this jump it is very high; at those who have little strength, the jump is few, and returns to a few; at those who have enough strength, the jump is many, and returns to many.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, it happens to some men that they are struck or dislocated, and the muscle of the spine is crushed by an abscess, and make sure it is not dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary that you examine it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And know that dislocations occur when they are pulled towards the shoulder, and make a difference between the diseased spine and the healthy one, and you will find a clear difference between them; and you will find at the top of the spine a hollow, and from there to the shoulder the top of the spine, as if it were some ones; and they cannot bring their hand back to their nose, nor move any movements; and if it is dislocated higher, if it is not hidden, because you can clearly see it at the shoulder; and this way of dislocation is not easy to put back, when it is new, or if the muscle is diseased.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the physician gently places his hand on the shoulder of the patient, then places his fingers on the acetabulum, and gently holds the joint at the top of the shoulder; he then releases his hand and extends it upwards, placing it below; if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in our hands just after, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; the physician should gently apply a soothing and softening ointment, like a decoction of aloe and fenugreek and honey in hot water, and then soothe the patient's shoulder; then he should put his hand on the patient's back, and place a lamen on the shoulder as high as possible, neither too soft nor too hard, and then place his foot on the lamen, and gently hold the head of the shoulder with his other hand, and trace the physician's hand on the shoulder; others may touch the shoulder with their hand to make sure it does not move; this shoulder is now returning, and if you see it in this way: and that you cause the present home to be greater than the shoulder; and it should be turned towards the chest, and bend the shoulder away from the acetabulum of the shoulder, and hold the acetabulum high up, so that the shoulder hangs downwards; and others may trace their hand on the shoulder towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too weak, and there is nothing heavy that can be done with them, then the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the reduction is also done in another way: and it is like finding a long pin in the ground, whose ends are similar to those of a tent peg, and not too large or too rough; then it is placed in the patient's shoulder, but if it has been bent too much, and the shoulder is too long, then the hand is extended from another part, forming the joint, and it returns to its place quickly; and if it does not return after all these things we have said, then this treatment must be followed: take two large and four small tent pegs, whose heads enter into one another at their end, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then place the forceps on the tip of the finger that is being operated on, so that it does not hurt the patient; then release the joint from the other hand; extend your arm over the long finger, and the helper's hand at the wrist of the thumb, then place the hand on the other side of the shield, and let the chest hang down from another part: the joint is now relieved.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is ready, in whatever way that may be, if you have to place the clamp on a thread of wool even, then place the powdered mill dust with incense and meadowsweet on all the shoulder blade and side, then tighten the clamp around the thread, and turn the string on the powder, and wrap your hand around the collar, and let your hand remain still.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	The following sentence is the translation: "And it is necessary to take only a little, as long as the limb is comfortable, because it heals faster; and then take more after the fourth or seventh day, and move it; and if it is tight and not softened, it is healthy.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	The following sentence is the translation: "And if the jointure is loose due to moisture or another cause, it is necessary to administer cauteries at three points, as it is placed before or in the chapter of cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	The following sentence is the translation: "And if you do everything, and after seven weeks, the jointure does not hold, and cannot raise the arm forward, then you should know that the nerve at the shoulder of the deltoid is compressed or extended or softened; and know that the jointure will never become tight in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The first line of the translation: "The dislocation that is towards the foot, and the ankles, or knees, if it is made by impulse, and extension of hands, and it is managed another hour; and it is cured as soon as it is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after the cure, if there is pain in the member, and later in movement, if the patient uses warm baths many times, as long as that pain is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the expensive dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	The joint that is expensive is dislocated and returns to its place many times; it becomes dislocated from all sides, and even in front and behind, and the dislocation is not well set, because one can see and feel it well; it becomes dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	When you join the sharp edge with your clean hand, if you can see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is fine, and cannot scratch the arm, nor touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset it always that the wound is closed and the vein is not cut, for if the vein is cut, it would be better to bring it back whole at all costs; and unexpectedly, it may not be possible to close all at once, especially when it is at the bottom; rather than other dislocations, it is more painful and sometimes death comes.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it is possible to return it, that you extend your hand to your two hands; and his arms are expanded, and his hands are stretched according to the edge of the shoulder, from the outside and inside, and you bind the joint with your fingers together, or at the root of the palm, as it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when it doubles its hand on its hand, and boasts of the root of the palm tree that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to the shoulder, then apply strong extension; and if two hands extend the arm, and hold it with two hands, so that it does not move at extension; then turn the arm in each part, then make a double loop of cloth long and wide; and when the patient feels the joint at the elbow, if no oil is applied to the joint, then form the joint with the joint, as it re-emerges; and when it is at the shoulder, put some dry linen with the suede on the shoulder, and form the arm, and let the hand remain in the groove of the malady, and leave a few fingers, then take it off.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is tight in its place, and it slips, and you see that the joint does not hold well, then re-tighten the splint and the joint, and leave it for some time until it is firmly fixed; then remove it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the dislocation of the joint, and it stays still, then he should bathe and rub gently, and press until it is calmed; or you can put a fat sheep's wool dressing on the joint, then leave it for one night and the bone, and let the ointment enter; when it is dry, remove the wool dressing, and then bathe or bain; and do this 2-3 times until it is healthy; if you see, if he puts on wet violet soaked with butter, and pulls it up; if it returns to its place.

des dislocations de la hainche	Of dislocations of the shoulder
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The shoulder joint and the shoulder blade joint are only dislocations, unlike other joints; and the shoulder joint is dislocated in four parts: front and back, and top and bottom; and more front than back, and less bottom than top.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai. de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the shoulder's dislocation

Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is if the ankle is swollen, and to try before reaching the part where it is dislocated: the hands should be light, and it should be gently extended by hand as soon as it is weak only.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, if you want to put the ankle back in its place: your hand should be light, and it should be gently extended by hand as soon as it is weak only. Then sit down at your right hand, and with your left hand pull the leg; then pull the foot twice, then raise it, and hold it well on the foot; and do this twice, if we have said, ending and raising the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, if it doesn't return, it resumes the dislocation, as it does; if it cannot be returned, I make the patient lie down on his back on the ground, and fasten one of his knees firmly against the ground, and let the other leg dangle freely; then trace the movement with your hand, and have others extend the foot to your hands or to the knee where it is located; then extend each of them equally, and the patient should be between the knees of the dislocated ankle to hold the ankle in place; then put the dislocation in your hands, and have others mark the sound leg at your side, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	When it reaches its point, if it is applied with plaster and allowed to dry, and the bandage forms, and the leg is held to the thigh, and the nerves which are below the ankle are not too tightly tied; then it is left on for II to III days, and if it becomes loose, then it is tightened again. Then it is removed at the end of the fourth or fifth day, and the patient is sent home with instructions to change the bandage every four days. If it comes loose before the end, it is only a matter of rebandaging.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms and comes, it is necessary that you open it if we have said elsewhere, as soon as it is healthy.
des dois	The first sentence to translate is "des
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if they are extended well in their work, it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in no way painful to the shoulder or arm, and it is possible that you can place the patient on his side or on his stomach, then put your foot on what opens these joints, then press with your foot on the parts that open, as it returns; and when it is equalized, if it does not open, then place a table under the shoulder at the head of the arm, then form the foot, and leave it for three days, then remove it; and let him rest, until he is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	together with wounds and dislocations
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When wounds and dislocations come together, and they are seen to be healing, often the patient dies: if you are not presumptuous in your treatment, it is because you have not used it long enough, or because you have not been pitiful and merciful, and timely; and begin with calming measures for abscesses, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, then immediately set the limb to the bone, unless the aposteme has already moved; and when the limb is at the bone, if there is swelling and inflammation, and the wound is healing, and it is not serious, then dress the wound with calming measures for abscesses, and treat the wound as we have said in simple diseases; and do not enter into a state of despair, according to what I have said, because this is what you deserve according to your creator, and through the knowledge of your arm and heart.
